The heap sweep also records two useful rejected points: `32G` MORI heap fails before step 1 with MORI static-heap exhaustion, while `64G` reaches step 1 but aborts in FSDP post-backward reduce with HSA out-of-resources/free-memory exhaustion. Read: MBS tuning materialized throughput uplift on the 12-layer probe, but MORI heap sizing and FSDP reduce memory headroom remain part of the batch-ladder constraint.

Low-intrusion MBS2 profile: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_additive_mori_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_heap40_steps2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_additive_mori_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_heap40_steps2_20260606.json) matches the batch-ladder shape and reaches step 2 at `3,619` tok/GPU/s, `14,476` node tok/s, `183.24 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `222.68 GiB` peak logged memory. Step-2 rank-max wall is `36.20s`: microbatch fwd/bwd `35.62s`, forward `8.45s`, loss `0.97s`, backward `20.82s`, and derived wrapper/residual `5.37s`. MORI rank-max GPU-event totals inside step 2 are owner-rank local VJP `4.33s`, `combine_dx` `1.49s`, grad-output dispatch `0.79s`, grad-output align `0.14s`, and dTopK/top-k return `0.15s`. Read: MBS2 lowers the 12-layer wall versus MBS1, but the next high-return work is still split across fused compact MoE owner backward/dX-return skew and the non-MORI backward wall from dense-fallback attention/projection/FSDP/autograd.

Dense fallback attention backward profile: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_dense_attention_backward_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_dense_attention_backward_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) adds opt-in `TORCHTITAN_DSV4_PROFILE_DENSE_ATTENTION_BACKWARD=1` timing at the guarded dense SDPA fallback boundary on the same active 12-layer MBS2/heap40 shape. It is diagnostic and slower: step 2 is `3,321` tok/GPU/s, `13,284` node tok/s, `168.13 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `222.82 GiB` peak memory. The useful split is step-2 dense attention records: actual SDPA backward grad totals `~7.97s/rank`, diagnostic recompute-forward totals `~2.06s/rank`, and the wrapper total is `~10.02s/rank`; per-layer dense fallback attention is roughly `0.83s` over 16 microbatches. In the same run, MORI owner local VJP max is `4.28s`, `combine_dx` max is `1.59s`, and grad-output dispatch max is `0.80s`. Read: the non-MORI wall is no longer shadowy; dense fallback attention backward is a first-order 12-layer bottleneck, so the next ladder must keep MoE/MORI owner-backward work in parallel with replacing guarded dense fallback by final sparse MLA/LI or another faster attention backward for compressed layers.

Shared-KV sparse MLA enablement A/B: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_sharedkv_sparse_enable_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_sharedkv_sparse_enable_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) tests the same active 12-layer MBS2/heap40 shape with `CANARY_SPARSE_MLA_MAX_SEQ_LEN=4096`, `shared_kv` query-recompute backward, and all compressed layers enabled. The default PyTorch LI/KL path is rejected at step 2 `707` tok/GPU/s and `35.81 TFLOPs/GPU`; selecting `CANARY_LI_KL_BACKEND=triton_tl_dot` recovers to `3,132` tok/GPU/s, `12,528` node tok/s, `158.56 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `213.94 GiB`, but still trails the retained guarded dense-fallback MBS2 run (`3,696` tok/GPU/s, `187.12 TFLOPs/GPU`). The sparse split shows C4 query-recompute is the real wall at about `110 ms/call` while C128 is about `32 ms/call`; the C128-only follow-up above is now promoted, while C4 remains the sparse-attention kernel rewrite target.

C4/C128 sparse-attention boundary gate: [`run_artifacts/sparse_mla_sharedkv_c4_c128_queryrecompute_profile_decision_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_mla_sharedkv_c4_c128_queryrecompute_profile_decision_20260606.json) measures the actual source-boundary Triton query-major shared-KV backward for the first C4 and C128 compressed layers with H64/D128 and valid N blocks. C4 layer 2 is `11.018 ms` full, `1.932 ms` no-dKV, and `2.839 ms` dKV checksum/sink, so the approximate global compressed dKV accumulation wall is `8.179 ms` over `805,044,224` modeled atomic/write elements. C128 layer 3 is `1.069 ms` full, `0.541 ms` no-dKV, and only `0.267 ms` approximate global dKV accumulation. The follow-up default-block C4 artifact [`run_artifacts/sparse_mla_sharedkv_queryrecompute_profile_c4_layer2_defaultblocks_s4096_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_mla_sharedkv_queryrecompute_profile_c4_layer2_defaultblocks_s4096_20260606.json) shows the old H16/N128 default was `41.409 ms` full with a `38.174 ms` approximate dKV accumulation wall, explaining why the earlier all-compressed e2e run reported C4 around `110 ms/call`. The materialized all-compressed H64/N64/D128 e2e run above promotes the block-shape fix, but the C4 rewrite still must preserve the fast query-major producer and replace the compressed dKV many-to-one accumulation/write epilogue.

Detailed owner-VJP profile: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_mori_owner_vjp_detail_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_mori_owner_vjp_detail_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) adds gated `TORCHTITAN_MORI_AITER_TIMING_GRANULARITY=expert_loop_detail` timing inside the retained compact `expert_loop` owner VJP. It is diagnostic and not promoted: step 2 drops to `3,460` tok/GPU/s, `13,840` node tok/s, `175.20 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `223.15 GiB` peak because per-expert CUDA events add overhead. The useful step-2 additive split is wall `37.86s`, microbatch fwd/bwd `37.31s`, forward `8.43s`, loss `0.98s`, backward `22.87s`, and wrapper residual `5.03s`. The MORI detail rank-max owner-VJP split is: wgrads `1.42s`, forward recompute `1.27s`, pack/scatter `0.72s`, xgrad/reduce `0.68s`, W2 dgrad+SwiGLU `0.57s`, and dTopK `0.45s`, while `combine_dx` remains visible at `1.44s`. Read: the next materializable MoE work should prioritize a fused compact grouped training backward for `dw1/dw2/dw3` plus forward-state reuse/recompute reduction, then xgrad/reduce and route pack/scatter. More blind MORI dispatch/combine knob sweeps are lower return than removing Python-issued per-expert GEMM loops and reducing owner-rank skew.

Expert-loop dX-first split A/B: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_expertloop_dxfirst_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_expertloop_dxfirst_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) adds a compact `expert_loop` owner-VJP split in `mori_aiter_moe.py`: compute local `dX`/`dTopK` first, return `dX`, then finish per-expert wgrads from compact late state. CPU and GPU BF16 parity pass against the original full expert-loop VJP. The active-shape `sync_dx_first` run completes the same 4-step MBS2 window at `GBS=128`, `S=4096`, heap40; steps 2-4 average `3,679` tok/GPU/s, `14,716` node tok/s, `186.29 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `225.22 GiB` peak logged memory. This is not promoted because it is slightly below the retained MBS2 steps-2-to-4 window (`3,696` tok/GPU/s, `187.12 TFLOPs/GPU`). The paired `asyncll_staged` attempts at heap40/42/48 all fail before step metrics with MORI static heap exhaustion while requesting `538,705,920` bytes, and heap64 is already known to starve FSDP post-backward headroom. Read: dx-first is a valid contract, but real overlap needs MORI buffer/allocation redesign or a fused compact owner-rank training backward, not more heap-size knob sweeps.

Expert-loop bucketed late-wgrad A/B: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_expertloop_dxfirst_bucketwgrad_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_expertloop_dxfirst_bucketwgrad_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) adds opt-in `TORCHTITAN_MORI_AITER_EXPERT_LOOP_WGRAD_MODE=bucket_bmm` for the dX-first late-wgrad finish. It buckets active experts by rounded token count, pads compact `x/scaled_dy/hidden/dgate/dup` slices, computes `dw2/dw1/dw3` with `torch.bmm`, and scatters back to per-expert gradients. CPU float32 and MI350 BF16 parity pass with max diff `0`, but the materialized active-shape 4xMI350 run is slower: steps 2-4 average `3,625` tok/GPU/s, `14,500` node tok/s, `183.54 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `224.54 GiB` peak logged memory. This is below both the retained MBS2 expert-loop sync run and the dX-first no-bucket run, so it is rejected. Read: padding/copy overhead in the bucketed wrapper erases the launch-consolidation benefit; the next MoE work should remove the Python owner-loop structure with fused compact grouped training backward rather than wrapping it in padded batches.

AITER TGMM late-wgrad A/B: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_expertloop_dxfirst_aiter_tgmm_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_expertloop_dxfirst_aiter_tgmm_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) adds opt-in `TORCHTITAN_MORI_AITER_EXPERT_LOOP_WGRAD_MODE=aiter_tgmm` for the same dX-first late-wgrad finish. CPU float32 and MI350 BF16 parity pass with max diff `0` for both AITER `ptgmm` and `nptgmm`, but the materialized active-shape 4xMI350 run regresses further: steps 2-4 average `2,969.33` tok/GPU/s, `11,877.33` node tok/s, `150.99 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `224.62 GiB` peak logged memory. This is `~19.7%` below retained MBS2 and `~18.1%` below the bucketed `torch.bmm` stopgap, so it is rejected. Read: using AITER TGMM as a late Python adapter does not remove the owner-loop structure or enough transient work; the next MoE branch must be a fused compact grouped owner-rank training backward or an AITER/CK training-backward contract that consumes AITER forward saved state directly.

AITER compact owner-VJP active-shape A/B: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_nptgmm_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_nptgmm_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) rejects the current `aiter_compact+nptgmm` adapter at the active 12-layer `MBS=2`, `GBS=128`, `S=4096`, `heap40` shape. It logs one invalid/slow step at `2,424.25` tok/GPU/s and `122.74 TFLOPs/GPU`, then OOMs in FP32 dTopK compact materialization while allocating another `3.00 GiB` with only `2.83 GiB` free. Read: keep the retained MBS2 12-layer candidate on `expert_loop` until a compact grouped owner VJP avoids this transient.

AITER compact memory-streaming follow-up: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_streamed_vjp_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_streamed_vjp_ab_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) adds bounded compact dTopK and streamed compact xgrad helpers in `mori_aiter_moe.py`. The patch proves two useful failure boundaries: dTopK streaming moves the OOM to compact xgrad, and streamed xgrad moves the cache-size-4 failure to FSDP post-backward headroom. With the transposed-weight cache disabled, the run completes 4 steps, but it is not valid or fast: loss/grad become NaN from step 2 onward and steps 2-4 average only `2,442.67` tok/GPU/s, `9,770.67` node tok/s, and `123.66 TFLOPs/GPU`, with `231.96 GiB` peak logged memory. The follow-up owner-VJP oracle [`run_artifacts/mori_aiter_owner_vjp_oracle_s4096_nptgmm_4x_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/mori_aiter_owner_vjp_oracle_s4096_nptgmm_4x_20260606.json) runs the retained `expert_loop`, `aiter_compact+nptgmm`, and dummy-stage1 VJP on the same real MORI-packed S4096 tensors; all ranks are finite and compact/dummy-stage1 match `expert_loop`. The timed oracle [`run_artifacts/mori_aiter_owner_vjp_timing_s4096_nptgmm_4x_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/mori_aiter_owner_vjp_timing_s4096_nptgmm_4x_20260606.json) further closes the compact adapter branch: compact recompute is dominated by streamed xgrad, route/sort, and forward-recompute overhead, while dummy-stage1 VJP is locally about `12.36 ms` mean / `12.80 ms` max. The grouped/full-xgrad follow-up [`run_artifacts/mori_aiter_owner_vjp_grouped_xgrad_s4096_nptgmm_4x_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/mori_aiter_owner_vjp_grouped_xgrad_s4096_nptgmm_4x_20260606.json) removes the streamed-xgrad stage locally and reduces compact VJP timing to about `1,691.44 ms` mean / `1,727.13 ms` max, but the materialized 12-layer run [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_groupedxgrad_c128_sparse_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_groupedxgrad_c128_sparse_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) is still rejected: `grad_norm` is NaN at step 1, loss is NaN from step 2, and steps 2-4 average only `2,482` tok/GPU/s, `9,928` node tok/s, and `125.68 TFLOPs/GPU`, with `226.73 GiB` peak logged memory. Read: the current AITER compact Python adapter is closed as a promotion branch because of integration/numerics/performance pressure, not because the isolated local owner-VJP math is wrong. The next MoE target remains a fused compact grouped owner-rank training backward or an AITER forward/backward contract that exposes or recomputes correct intermediates inside the fused owner without the adapter's transient slabs.

AITER compact grouped-xgrad `ptgmm` diagnosis: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_groupedxgrad_ptgmm_gradscan_materialization_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_groupedxgrad_ptgmm_gradscan_materialization_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) adds a pre-clip gradient scan and an A/B on the compact AITER expert wgrad op. The failed `nptgmm` one-step repro has finite loss but nonfinite expert wgrads before clipping: rank 1 first hits `layers.0.moe.experts.w3`, while ranks 0 and 3 first hit `layers.6.moe.experts.w2`; the finite max saturates at BF16 max (`3.389e38`). Switching only the compact wgrad op to `ptgmm` makes all four pre-clip scans finite. The materialized 4-step `ptgmm` run is valid, with steps 2-4 average `3,634` tok/GPU/s, `14,536` node tok/s, `184.0 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `222.39 GiB` peak logged memory, but it is still about `6.04%` slower than the retained C128 sparse `expert_loop` candidate (`3,867.67` tok/GPU/s, `195.84 TFLOPs/GPU`, `218.42 GiB`). Read: avoid `nptgmm` for compact expert wgrads at this shape; `ptgmm` rescues numerics but does not promote the Python compact adapter. The next MoE path remains a fused or FP32-safe compact grouped owner VJP, not more adapter-level knobs.

AITER compact `ptgmm` profile follow-up: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_ptgmm_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_ptgmm_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) runs the finite compact `ptgmm` path with additive and MORI owner-VJP detail timing. It completes two steps; step 2 logs `3,710` tok/GPU/s, `14,840` node tok/s, `187.83 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `222.20 GiB` peak memory. The additive step-2 split is wall `35.31s`, microbatch fwd/bwd `34.74s`, forward `7.84s`, loss `0.98s`, backward `20.50s`, and wrapper/residual `5.42s`. The post-warm MORI timing window attributes owner local VJP rank-total max `5.94s`, with compact-stage rank-total maxima dominated by `prepare_ops 1.50s`, `wgrad 1.43s`, `recompute_forward 1.15s`, and `xgrad/reduce 0.87s`; route pack is only `0.03s`. Read: the valid compact adapter is still structurally wrong for promotion. The wall is Python/adapter prepare, recompute, and grouped training-gradient work, not route metadata; keep the retained C128 sparse `expert_loop` candidate and move toward a fused or FP32-safe compact grouped owner-rank training backward.

AITER compact `ptgmm` expert-recompute diagnostic: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_ptgmm_expertrecompute_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_aiter_compact_ptgmm_expertrecompute_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs2_20260606.json) adds opt-in `TORCHTITAN_MORI_AITER_COMPACT_RECOMPUTE_MODE=expert_loop`, skipping the grouped-GMM transpose-prepare contract for compact forward recompute while retaining compact `ptgmm` wgrads and grouped xgrad. The two-step profile reaches step 2 at `3,903` tok/GPU/s, `15,612` node tok/s, `197.60 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `218.41 GiB` peak logged memory. Versus the previous compact `ptgmm` profile, this is `+5.20%` tok/s, `+5.16%` TFLOPs/GPU, `-1.75s` step wall, and `-3.79 GiB` peak memory. It is a positive diagnostic but not promoted: the timing sidecars were appended in the remote workdir, the prepare stage did not shrink cleanly enough to claim transpose avoidance as the root cause, and this is still a two-step profiled run. The next gate is a clean non-profile 4-step or 6-step materialization before replacing the retained C128 sparse `expert_loop` candidate.

The follow-up unique-sidecar profile above supersedes the appended-sidecar caveat for attribution: on the exact retained candidate shape, compact `prepare_ops` is only `0.0015s` rank-total max in step 2, while owner local VJP, C128 shared-KV query-recompute, and the wrapper/residual bucket remain the visible walls.

## Goal

Assuming the single-layer fwd/bwd kernel candidate is usable, pursue a first 4xMI350 or 8xMI350 TorchTitan DeepSeek-V4 pretraining canary focused on training-system integration rather than more single-layer math.

Start with the minimum distributed shape: `TP=1`, `PP=1`, `CP=1`, `FSDP=4/8`, `EP=4/8`. Defer TP until memory or collectives require it, since MLA/MoE tensor partitioning adds major complexity. The first target is a correctness-first BF16 canary with real learned routing, EP token dispatch/return, FSDP sharding, activation recompute, gradient accumulation, checkpoint/resume, and loss movement on synthetic or small-token data.

The canary must have DeepSeek-V4 model identity. The existing DeepSeek-V3 16B run remains useful for proving distributed plumbing only; it must not be promoted as the DeepSeek-V4 canary or used as the config source for final reporting.

The main remaining blockers are TorchTitan model integration, dynamic EP routing/all-to-all, distributed optimizer support, PyTorch reference coverage, and checkpointing. The current milestone uses AdamW so the 8xMI350 canary can focus on distributed training behavior and end-to-end performance. Muon is future work after the AdamW path is stable.

Performance should be reported first as the 4xMI350 or 8xMI350 end-to-end canary target: `~12.2k` tok/GPU/s at `S=4096`, `GBS=128`, with MBS tunable for best sustained throughput. For the 4x shape this is `~48.8k` node tok/s. The next active promotion focus is `flash_12layer_ceiling_probe`: first 12 recipe compress ratios `(1,1,4,128,4,128,4,128,4,128,4,128)`, i.e. 2 dense layers plus 5 C4A layers and 5 C128A layers at full dimensions. In the local TorchTitan WIP, dense/uncompressed layers are encoded as `compress_ratio=0`, so the code-level ratio list is `[0,0,4,128,4,128,4,128,4,128,4,128]`. The local reference snapshot is `sources/references/ascend-cann-recipes-train/`, imported from:

- `https://atomgit.com/cann/cann-recipes-train/blob/master/llm_pretrain/deepseekv4/README.md`
- `https://atomgit.com/cann/cann-recipes-train/blob/master/docs/llm_pretrain/deepseek-v4_torchtitan_npu_autofuse.md`

The active 4xMI350 canary target is:

| Metric | 4xMI350 target | Current retained 4x candidate |
| --- | ---: | ---: |
| Node throughput | `~48.8k` tok/s | `~50,281.3` tok/s |
| Per-GPU throughput | `~12.2k` tok/s | `12,570.33` tok/s |
| Sequence length | `4096` | `4096` |
| Global batch size | `128` | `128` |
| Microbatch size | tunable | `4` |
| Late-step TFLOPs/GPU | report-only | `237.19` |
| Implied FLOP/token | report-only | `~18.87 GFLOP/token` (`~0.01887 TFLOP/token`) for this 4-layer canary |
| Peak logged memory | report-only | `115.04 GiB` |
| Next promotion focus | `flash_12layer_ceiling_probe` | Current lower-memory top-8 standard-EP helper + owner-compact hot rows steps 2-6: `8,051.75` tok/GPU/s, `407.6725 TFLOPs/GPU`, `194.90 GiB` |
| Artifact | n/a | `run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_saved_dispatch_reuse_ab_20260605.json` |

The older Ascend-normalized `~277 TFLOPs/GPU` proxy remains useful as aspirational parity context, not the current 4x pass/fail gate. With the retained 4-layer `~18.87 GFLOP/token` (`~0.01887 TFLOP/token`) accounting, the current `~12.2k` tok/GPU/s gate maps to about `230 TFLOPs/GPU`, while `~277 TFLOPs/GPU` would imply roughly `14.7k` tok/GPU/s. Do not reuse this FLOP/token blindly for the 12-layer ceiling probe: TorchTitan FLOP/token accounting is model-shape dependent, so 12-layer promotion should lead with tok/GPU/s, node tok/s, step time, memory, and then its own measured TFLOPs/GPU. Ascend TorchTitan-NPU/CANN AutoFuse reports DeepSeek-V4-Flash BF16 4K training on 64 Atlas A3 cards with `TP=1`, `PP=1`, `VPP=1`, `EP=128`, `FSDP=128`, `MBS=1`, and `GBS=1024`; treat the older `1100` tokens/GPU/s source anchor as reference context. For the old 8xMI350 parity proxy:

| Metric | 8xMI350 target |
| --- | ---: |
| Target TFLOPs/GPU | `~277` |
| Implied MI350X BF16-peak MFU | `~12.0%` |
| Derived per-GPU throughput using retained FLOPs/token accounting | `~14,640` training tokens/GPU/s |
| Derived 8-GPU node throughput | `~117,122` training tokens/s |
| Effective batch shape matching Ascend tokens/GPU | `MBS=1`, `S=4096`, `GBS=128` |
| Tokens per step at `GBS=128` | `524,288` tokens |
| Derived step time at target and `GBS=128` | `~4.48 s` |

For a 4xMI350 slice, keep the same `~277 TFLOPs/GPU` target and halve the node total: derived `~58,561` training tokens/s/node, `GBS=64`, `262,144` tokens/step, and the same derived `~4.48 s/step` under the retained FLOPs/token accounting.

The one-MI350 single-layer microbench anchors are `24.9 ms` full layer fwd+bwd+grads at `S=4096`, `3.6 ms` forward attention, and `12.9 ms` for the whole MoE layer's routed expert GEMM family fwd+bwd in one batched/grouped call across all experts. The MoE anchor is not a per-expert latency.

The practical ladder is: tiny 8-GPU PyTorch-only DSv4 stack, full-dim 1-layer custom-kernel stack with fixed router, few-layer dynamic-router EP stack, optimizer plus checkpoint/resume, then full 43-layer Flash-shape canary at short sequence before attempting `B=1 S=4096`. Success for this milestone is clean distributed training behavior with metrics reported against the above target; matching Ascend parity is an aspirational comparison, not the pass/fail bar for the first canary.

## Layout

- `changesets/`: local patches or patch notes required to reproduce the experiment.
- `docs/`: active notes, roadmap, and status checkpoints.
- `launchers/`: canonical rerun scripts once a first AMD canary shape is selected.
- `run_artifacts/`: compact pins and artifact pointers; raw logs, checkpoints, and traces stay outside the repo.
- `targets/`: model/config contracts for the AMD pretrain canary surfaces.
- `tools/`: host-side helper scripts if source comparison or launch preparation needs them.

The vendored source trees now live at repo root in `../../projects/` and `../../references/`;
see [`docs/source_migration_20260613.md`](docs/source_migration_20260613.md).
Source trees are plain tracked snapshots, not nested Git repos or submodules.

## Current Notes

- MORI EP/MoE 4x retained canary: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_saved_dispatch_reuse_ab_20260605.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_saved_dispatch_reuse_ab_20260605.json) is the current best sustained materialized 4xMI350 result. Shape: `TP=1`, `PP=1`, `CP=1`, `FSDP=4`, `EP=4`, `MBS=4`, `GBS=128`, `GA=8`, `S=4096`, no activation checkpointing, AdamW, MORI+AITER fused forward, routed backward, compact `expert_loop` local VJP, saved forward dispatch reuse, Triton SwiGLU, compact xgrad, expandable allocator. Steps 4-6 average `12,570.33` tok/GPU/s, `~50,281.3` node tok/s, and `237.19 TFLOPs/GPU`; peak logged memory is `115.04 GiB`. The no-save expert-loop control averaged `12,006.67` tok/GPU/s, `~48,026.7` node tok/s, and `227.19 TFLOPs/GPU`, so reusing compact AITER forward dispatch state is a materialized `~4.4%` late-step TFLOPs uplift at the cost of about `+3.79 GiB` peak logged memory. The follow-up profile in [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_saved_dispatch_profile_4x_s4096_20260605.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_saved_dispatch_profile_4x_s4096_20260605.json) shows saved-dispatch overhead itself is tiny; the remaining MORI wall is the Python per-expert owner VJP plus dX-return wait/skew. The paired route-padding profile shows the prior padded owner VJP did `22.03x` mean and `44.204x` max zero-padding work under learned-router imbalance, so the MoE wall is route-imbalance-induced padded compute/transient materialization plus dX-return skew, not raw MORI collective bandwidth alone. The next production target is compact/AITER-owned saved forward state plus fused grouped owner-rank training backward, replacing the Python per-expert loop.
- 12-layer ceiling-probe smoke: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_smoke_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs1_step1_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_smoke_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs1_step1_20260606.json) is the first materialized active-target run. The remote `check-config` on `do-vunguyen-mi350-gpu` reports `model_spec deepseek_v4 flash_12layer_ceiling_probe`, `model_layers=12`, and parsed code ratios `[0,0,4,128,4,128,4,128,4,128,4,128]`, corresponding to the recipe shorthand `(1,1,4,128,4,128,4,128,4,128,4,128)`. The one-step 4xMI350 run uses `TP=PP=CP=1`, `FSDP=4`, `EP=4`, `S=4096`, `GBS=128`, `MBS=1`, no activation checkpointing, checkpoint-free, AdamW, MORI+AITER fused forward, routed `expert_loop` backward, saved forward dispatch reuse, Triton SwiGLU, compact xgrad, and expandable allocator. It passes one optimizer step with finite loss/grad norm (`loss=12.19550`, `grad_norm=12.625`) and no checkpoint payload. Mean step-1 metrics are `1,745.75` tok/GPU/s, `~6,983` node tok/s, `88.41 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `172.51 GiB` peak logged memory, about `0.143x` of the `12.2k` tok/GPU/s target. It is not promoted because it is a single warm step and because the compressed layers still hit the S4096 guarded dense fallback rather than final sparse MLA/LI performance.
- 12-layer ceiling-probe additive/MORI profile: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_additive_mori_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs1_steps2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_additive_mori_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs1_steps2_20260606.json) is the first same-shape timing decomposition for the active target. Shape matches the smoke: `TP=PP=CP=1`, `FSDP=4`, `EP=4`, `S=4096`, `GBS=128`, `MBS=1`, no activation checkpointing, checkpoint-free, AdamW, MORI+AITER fused forward, routed `expert_loop` backward, saved forward dispatch reuse, compact xgrad, expandable allocator. Step 2 reports `2,473` tok/GPU/s, `~9,892` node tok/s, `125.23 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `202.17 GiB` peak memory, about `0.203x` of the `12.2k` tok/GPU/s target. The additive step-2 wall is `52.97s`: child buckets are backward `27.62s`, forward `12.26s`, loss `1.44s`, and a derived microbatch wrapper/residual of `11.04s`. MORI/AITER step-2 GPU-event totals show owner-rank local VJP `6.49s`, `combine_dx` `1.36s`, grad-output dispatch `0.95s`, and grad-output align `0.19s`. Read: MoE/MORI remains a high-return target, but it is not the whole 12-layer wall; the next decomposition must split the remaining dense-fallback attention/projection/FSDP/backward-wrapper work.
- 12-layer dense-linear/loss profile: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_dense_linear_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs1_steps2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_dense_linear_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs1_steps2_20260606.json) runs the same active target with opt-in custom-autograd dense linear timing. It is intentionally diagnostic and slower: step 2 drops to `2,276` tok/GPU/s, `115.23 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `201.38 GiB` peak memory. Step-2 additive wall is `57.57s`, with backward `32.21s`, forward `12.22s`, loss `1.46s`, and wrapper/residual `11.10s`. Dense/loss sidecars attribute rank-max totals of loss `1.43s`, attention projection backward `1.47s`, shared-expert dense backward `1.11s`, and router backward `0.06s`. MORI main backward stages are still about `8.22s` rank-max (`6.37s` owner VJP plus dX/grad dispatch/top-k return), but backward minus MORI remains `~24.0s`, and backward minus MORI plus measured dense non-loss remains `~21.36s`. Read: the next decomposition has to split dense inner attention, FSDP/autograd synchronization, and wrapper/context overhead; do not promote this run as throughput evidence.
- 12-layer torch-profiler scope profile: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_torchprof_scope_profile_readout_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs1_steps2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_torchprof_scope_profile_readout_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs1_steps2_20260606.json) and raw summary [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_torchprof_scope_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs1_steps2_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_torchprof_scope_profile_4x_s4096_gbs128_mbs1_steps2_20260606.json) run the same active target with Torch profiler enabled and the dense-linear custom wrapper disabled. It completes two steps with finite loss movement `12.30625 -> 9.41330`, but logged step-2 throughput is only `1,241` tok/GPU/s and `62.83 TFLOPs/GPU` because trace export contaminates log-to-log timing; do not use it as throughput evidence. The additive step-2 compute wall is `62.06s`, with `61.32s` in the 32-microbatch fwd/bwd loop: forward `13.70s`, loss `1.52s`, backward `34.76s`, and wrapper residual `11.34s`. The valid trace is iteration 1 only; iteration 2 was overwritten by a tiny shutdown profiler trace, so the artifact combines step-1 trace ranking with step-2 sidecars. Step-1 trace rank-medians show kernel families `other=21.19s`, GEMM `8.63s`, copy `7.92s`, RCCL/NCCL `5.27s`, and unattributed GEMM `7.82s`. Step-2 sidecars show MORI local expert-loop VJP `12.01s` median / `12.93s` max, `combine_dx` `2.01s` median / `3.24s` max, grad dispatch `0.86s`, and chunked CE loss `1.48s`. Read: MORI/MoE remains the largest named optimization target, but after MoE return and loss there is still roughly `15-18s` of backward wall to split across dense-fallback attention/projection, FSDP/autograd synchronization, and allocator/free behavior.
- 12-layer torch-profiler deep-op trace mining: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_torchprof_deep_ops_readout_4x_s4096_step1_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_torchprof_deep_ops_readout_4x_s4096_step1_20260606.json), backed by [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_torchprof_deep_ops_allranks_step1_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_dsv4_flash12_torchprof_deep_ops_allranks_step1_20260606.json), mines exact CPU op and GPU kernel names from the same valid step-1 traces. This fixes the main blind spot from scope-only attribution: the attention backward kernels are not owned by the forward `dsv4.attention.*` record-function ranges. Per rank, `bwd_kernel_dk_dv.kd` appears exactly `384` times (`12 layers * 32` microsteps) at `5.74s` median, `bwd_kernel_dq.kd` appears exactly `384` times at `2.68s` median, and `attn_fwd.kd` appears exactly `384` times at `2.03s` median. That explains a large part of backward-minus-MORI and promotes dense-fallback attention backward replacement/avoidance to the next optimization tier after fused owner-rank MoE backward. Other visible CPU/autograd/FSDP buckets are real but smaller in this trace: `record_param_comms` `6.87s` median, `RegisterPostBackwardFunctionBackward` `5.97s`, `MmBackward0` `5.61s`, `fsdp::chunk_cat` `4.28s`, and `c10d::barrier` `3.69s`. Next action: add low-intrusion attention-backward scopes or custom-autograd boundaries so the `bwd_kernel_dk_dv/dq` wall can be split by layer/compress ratio, and then measure whether restoring final sparse MLA/LI backward for C4/C128 layers materializes into 12-layer e2e uplift.
- Ascend MoE/EP lesson mapping: [`changesets/torchtitan_mori_aiter_ascend_moe_ep_lessons.md`](changesets/torchtitan_mori_aiter_ascend_moe_ep_lessons.md) and [`run_artifacts/ascend_moe_ep_lessons_amd_mapping_20260605.json`](run_artifacts/ascend_moe_ep_lessons_amd_mapping_20260605.json) pin the source-backed read from the Ascend TorchTitan-NPU/CANN recipe. The relevant lessons are pure FSDP plus large EP, independent FSDP/EP communication domains, native token permute/unpermute, native grouped expert GEMM, compact route metadata instead of full routed-output saves, AutoFuse-style vector clutter removal, and finer recompute as future work. AMD mapping: keep AITER fused forward, reuse compact MORI/AITER dispatch state, avoid padded slabs, and implement an AITER/CK fused grouped owner-rank training backward that either exposes raw `gate`/`up`/`hidden`/compact-output state or recomputes `gate`/`up` once inside the fused VJP.
- AITER compact owner-VJP diagnostic: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_aiter_compact_vjp_materialization_20260605.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_aiter_compact_vjp_materialization_20260605.json) proves the compact AITER grouped-GEMM VJP branch is executable at the same `4xMI350`, `S=4096`, `GBS=128`, `MBS=4` target shape, but it is not promoted. The uncached branch averaged `11,564.67` tok/GPU/s and `218.82 TFLOPs/GPU` over steps 4-6 with `125.25 GiB` peak memory. A transposed-weight LRU cache improved this to `12,246.0` tok/GPU/s and `231.93 TFLOPs/GPU`, but memory rose to `134.10 GiB`, still behind the retained expert-loop baseline at `12,570.33` tok/GPU/s, `237.19 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `115.04 GiB`. Profile medians remain dominated by backward forward-recompute, wgrad, xgrad, and prepare/layout work, so the production direction is AITER-forward-compatible compact saved intermediates or a fused grouped owner-rank training backward rather than a backward adapter that recomputes all forward intermediates.
- AITER stage1 capture probe: [`run_artifacts/aiter_stage1_capture_s4096_h4096_i2048_e64_top6_20260605.json`](run_artifacts/aiter_stage1_capture_s4096_h4096_i2048_e64_top6_20260605.json) validates the concrete AITER two-stage forward path at the local owner-expert shape (`tokens=4096`, `hidden=4096`, `intermediate=2048`, `experts=64`, `topk=6`). Manual `moe_sorting -> ck_moe_stage1 -> ck_moe_stage2` matches public `fused_moe` (`max_abs_diff=3.81e-6`, finite outputs), exposes post-SwiGLU `stage1` hidden `[4096,6,2048]` (`96 MiB`), and times at `2.29 ms` median versus `2.46 ms` for public fused MoE in the probe. This means saved stage1 is technically viable without replacing the fast AITER schedule, but it is still insufficient full backward state: raw `gate`, raw `up`, and per-route W2 output are still missing. The next MoE branch should expose those from AITER/CK or implement a fused owner VJP that recomputes gate/up once internally.
- AITER stage1-saved TorchTitan bridge: [`changesets/torchtitan_mori_aiter_stage1_saved_forward.md`](changesets/torchtitan_mori_aiter_stage1_saved_forward.md), [`run_artifacts/mori_aiter_stage1_saved_vjp_parity_s4096_dummy_4x_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/mori_aiter_stage1_saved_vjp_parity_s4096_dummy_4x_20260606.json), and [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_aiter_stage1_saved_dummy_target_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_aiter_stage1_saved_dummy_target_20260606.json) add an opt-in `TORCHTITAN_MORI_AITER_FORWARD_MODE=aiter_stage1_saved` path that mirrors AITER's real BF16 two-stage fused MoE forward and saves compact post-SwiGLU stage1 state for routed local owner VJP. The original global-id stage1 target run is still demoted in [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_aiter_stage1_saved_target_demote_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_mori_aiter_stage1_saved_target_demote_20260606.json) because it produced NaN gradients/loss. The corrected dummy-local route contract maps nonlocal MORI routes to one zero dummy AITER expert while preserving the global route table for backward; it passes S4096 owner-VJP parity against compact recompute and the retained expert-loop oracle on all ranks. The fixed target-shape 4xMI350 `S=4096`, `GBS=128`, `MBS=4` run completes six finite steps and clears the current token gate at steps 4-6 average `11,887.33` tok/GPU/s, `47,549.33` node tok/s, and `224.93 TFLOPs/GPU`, but it is not promoted because the retained expert-loop saved-dispatch canary is faster and lower memory at `12,570.33` tok/GPU/s, `237.19 TFLOPs/GPU`, and `115.04 GiB` versus `151.46 GiB` peak logged memory. The timing artifact [`run_artifacts/mori_aiter_owner_vjp_timing_s4096_nptgmm_4x_20260606.json`](run_artifacts/mori_aiter_owner_vjp_timing_s4096_nptgmm_4x_20260606.json) shows dummy-stage1 forward at `3.85 ms` mean and dummy-stage1 owner VJP at `12.36 ms` mean / `12.80 ms` max for one active S4096 owner-rank sample. Read: saved-stage1 is a valid wiring/probe branch, but the production target remains a fused grouped owner-rank training backward that avoids both the large post-SwiGLU stage1 save and the Python compact adapter.
- 8x target-shape step-burst diagnosis: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_8x_step_burst_diagnosis_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_8x_step_burst_diagnosis_20260604.json) compares six-step no-profile gates for no-AC plus expandable allocator, full-AC default allocator, and full-AC plus expandable allocator. Step 2 is consistently a burst, not a stable reporting number. The old best sustained 8x candidate before MORI compact owner VJP was no-AC plus expandable allocator at `64.91 TFLOPs/GPU` averaged over steps 4-6; the full-AC allocator-expanded control settles at `47.91 TFLOPs/GPU`, so allocator configuration alone does not explain the slowdown. Use late-step or multi-step averages for promotion decisions.
- Actual-LI prepacked route-consumption timing: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_dkv_prepacked_route_consumption.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_dkv_prepacked_route_consumption.py), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_prepacked_route_consumption_metadata_s4096_layer2_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_prepacked_route_consumption_metadata_s4096_layer2_20260603.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_prepacked_route_consumption_scalar_s4096_layer2_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_prepacked_route_consumption_scalar_s4096_layer2_20260603.json), and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_prepacked_route_consumption_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_prepacked_route_consumption_decision_20260603.json) close the next gate for the group-owned compressed-dKV candidate. The sorted pair-list metadata walk is `~0.02 ms`, the segment-start walk is `~0.02 ms`, and the optional one-D-lane scalar input walk through `q/dO/probs/grad_logits` is `0.58-0.68 ms` at S4096 layer 2. This promotes the branch from "metadata promising" to a real speedup candidate: prepack actual LI routes, keep query-major contribution production, perform tile-local grouped/segmented D16 reduction, then emit reduced dKV atomics or compact partial rows. The remaining risk is specifically the full D16 MFMA accumulator plus in-tile grouped/segmented reduction; route packing/traversal is no longer the suspected wall.
- Sparse dKV dense-like reduction contract: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_dense_like_kernel_contract_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_dense_like_kernel_contract_20260603.json) captures the current answer to why dense attention does not suffer the same global-atomic shape even though it has the same mathematical many-to-one reduction. Dense backward treats `dV=P^T dO` and `dK=dS^TQ` as owned output-tile GEMM reductions; the current sparse path instead emits about `805M` scalar atomic adds into indirect compressed groups. The retained path to make sparse dKV dense-like is now `query-major compact keyed producer -> rocPRIM reduce_by_key`: route packing is `0.52-0.54 ms`, compact reduce-by-key is `0.44 ms` when sorted or `1.1 ms` with sort/reorder/reduce, and the open budget is the producer. To beat the `8.0-8.8 ms` atomic wall, the producer must be below about `6.3-7.0 ms`; to move toward the old sparse-backward envelope, it should be closer to `3-4 ms`. Closed branches remain detached raw ScatterAdd, panel-owned contribution production, local-table compact emit, and small hot-group tail-atomic reducers.
- Sparse dKV prepack-to-dense-like decision: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_prepack_to_dense_like_gap_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_prepack_to_dense_like_gap_decision_20260603.json) records why cheap prepacking is necessary but not sufficient. The route can now be sorted/segmented cheaply, but every measured kernel that changed compressed groups into the producer owner while losing query-major MFMA reuse regressed at S4096: pair-slot LDS reducers are `~18 ms`, segment-owned scalar CTAs are `44.6 ms`, row-leader/persistent grouped schedules are `>130 ms`, and panel-owned D16 contribution sinks are `111-130 ms`. The promoted next kernel is therefore `query_major_segmented_mfma_dkv_producer_v1`: preserve the fast query-major contribution loop, add lane/warp/block segmented accumulation before global writes, emit compact `(compressed_group, D16)` partial rows, then use the already-cheap compact reducer.
- Sparse dKV group-outer-loop decision: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_group_outer_loop_reuse_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_group_outer_loop_reuse_decision_20260603.json) closes the question of simply making compressed group the outermost producer loop after prepack. Prepack gives cheap membership lookup, but the measured `32x256` and `32x512` group segments have `overall_pair_over_unique_token_x=1.0`, `duplicate_token_segments=0`, and `max_pairs_per_token_per_segment_p99=1.0`: every group segment has at most one selected row per token. That makes group segments excellent reducer/writeback owners (`12.34x` to `23.81x` write reduction) but poor contribution-production owners, because they cannot reuse a token's `q/dO` across selected slots. The retained contract is still group-aware writeback inside a query-major MFMA producer, not group-outermost contribution production.
- Sparse dKV MoE-routing lesson and two-level producer plan: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/plan_sparse_dkv_two_level_segmented_producer.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/plan_sparse_dkv_two_level_segmented_producer.py), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_two_level_segmented_producer_plan_s4096_layer2_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_two_level_segmented_producer_plan_s4096_layer2_20260603.json), and [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_moe_routing_lessons_and_two_level_plan_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_moe_routing_lessons_and_two_level_plan_20260603.json) turn the MoE analogy into a kernel contract. The transferable MoE lesson is route pack plus compact routed ownership; the non-transferable part is expert-owned compute. For sparse dKV, query-major `q/dO` reuse must own contribution production while compressed group owns reduction/writeback. The new two-level planner sizes `query-major micro producer -> segmented micro rows -> selected-tile merge -> final compact reduce`. At `32x512/K64`, the micro producer only reaches `3.43x` reduction and emits `~952 MiB` of micro partial stream before a `6.95x` tile merge; at `32x512/K128`, it reaches `6.37x` with `~512 MiB` micro stream before a `3.74x` tile merge. Decision: prototype `K128` first, starting with the safer `32x256` gate, then `32x512`; producer+tile-merge+final-reduce must beat the `8.0-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic dKV wall including route-pack cost.
- Sparse dKV selected-tile compact partial-store runtime gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_dkv_active_list_triton.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_dkv_active_list_triton.py) now adds `--kernel dot_k_compact_micro_partial_store`, which keeps the fast query-major `tl.dot` producer but writes compact partial rows per `(seq tile, selected-key tile)` before final `index_add`. S128 layer-2 parity passes in [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_partial_store_s128_layer2_sc16_sb32_d16h64k32_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_partial_store_s128_layer2_sc16_sb32_d16h64k32_20260603.json) with max diff `0.0697`. The hard S4096 layer-2 timings in [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_partial_store_s4096_layer2_sc32_sb128_d16h64k64_timing10_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_partial_store_s4096_layer2_sc32_sb128_d16h64k64_timing10_20260603.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_partial_store_s4096_layer2_sc32_sb256_d16h64k64_timing10_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_partial_store_s4096_layer2_sc32_sb256_d16h64k64_timing10_20260603.json), and [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_compact_micro_partial_store_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_compact_micro_partial_store_decision_20260603.json) reject this as a latency promotion: `K128` full/emit medians are `9.35/8.82 ms`, `K256` is `8.64/8.33 ms`, versus the same-tuple sparse-atomic gate at `8.01 ms` and seq-tile compact partial full at `8.54 ms`. The selected-tile split is a useful diagnostic, but it still performs one global partial load/store per valid selected KxD contribution; the next kernel must reduce inside the producer with lane/warp/block segmented accumulation before global memory, not add another compact partial slab.
- Sparse dKV compact-micro merge gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_dkv_active_list_triton.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_dkv_active_list_triton.py), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_merged_partial_store_s128_layer2_sc16_sb128_d16h64k32_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_merged_partial_store_s128_layer2_sc16_sb128_d16h64k32_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_merged_partial_store_s512_layer2_sc32_sb128_d16h64k64_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_merged_partial_store_s512_layer2_sc32_sb128_d16h64k64_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_merged_partial_store_s4096_layer2_sc32_sb128_d16h64k64_timing_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_merged_partial_store_s4096_layer2_sc32_sb128_d16h64k64_timing_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_compact_micro_merged_partial_store_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_compact_micro_merged_partial_store_decision_20260604.json) close the obvious two-stage reducer follow-up. The new `dot_k_compact_micro_merged_partial_store` mode keeps the query-major dot-K producer, writes compact micro rows, then merges those rows into seq-tile compact rows before the final fold. S128 and S512 parity pass (`max diff 0.0696/0.0717`), and the S4096 merge-only kernel is modest at `0.914 ms`. But the full S4096 path is slower than the retained compact-micro baseline: `10.79 ms` full and `8.95 ms` emit-only versus baseline `9.35/8.82 ms`. Decision: a separate micro-to-seq merge is useful evidence but not the next speed path; the reducer has to move inside the producer before global micro-row writes, or LI/compressor dKV must be fused so the raw selected KxD write never happens.
- Sparse dKV expanded in-producer window decision: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_inproducer_window_reduction_plan_s4096_layer2_expanded_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_inproducer_window_reduction_plan_s4096_layer2_expanded_20260603.json) and [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_inproducer_window_expanded_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_inproducer_window_expanded_decision_20260603.json) select the next runtime gate after the selected-tile partial-store rejection. Same-slot/per-topk-column accumulation stays near `1.03-1.07x`, so it is not a useful implementation target. Full local segmentation reaches the needed envelope only at wide windows: `32x512` gives `23.81x` write reduction with `66,029` reduced rows, `64x256` gives `24.47x` with `64,261` rows, and `64x512` gives `47.25x` with `33,274` rows but much wider route tiles. Decision: first real segmented producer gate should be `token_window=32`, `selected_block=512`, then `64x256`; compare full producer+reducer time against the `8.01 ms` sparse-atomic wall. Dense active-group tables or per-contribution LDS stores remain rejected because p50 touched groups are still about `516-520` and p99 is near all `1024` groups.
- TileLang sparse-MQA backward reference gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_reference.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_reference.py), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_reference_s4096_kv1024_topk512_d256_synthetic_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_reference_s4096_kv1024_topk512_d256_synthetic_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_reference_s4096_kv1024_topk512_h32_d512_synthetic_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_reference_s4096_kv1024_topk512_h32_d512_synthetic_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_reference_s4096_kv1024_topk512_h64_d512_headsplit32_synthetic_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_reference_s4096_kv1024_topk512_h64_d512_headsplit32_synthetic_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_reference_atomic_gate_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_reference_atomic_gate_decision_20260604.json) close the "try straight TileLang first" branch. The vendored Miles DSv4 TileLang forward and backward cannot compile at target `H64/D512/topk512` on MI350 because dynamic shared memory exceeds the `163,840` byte block limit (`206,848` for forward, `204,800` for backward; `block_size=16` worsens to `219,104`). The nice `7.59 ms` point is only `S4096,H64,D256` half-D. At target width, `S4096,H32,D512` is `14.05 ms` for half-heads and the concrete `H64/D512` `head_split=32` run is `28.11 ms`, slower than the current `8.01 ms` Triton sparse-atomic dKV wall. Decision: do not promote the straight `T.atomic_addx4` reference into TorchTitan; TileLang remains useful only if we rewrite the schedule to fit shared memory and add in-producer segmented dKV reduction before global atomics.
- TileLang continuation gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_diagnostic.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_diagnostic.py), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_nodkv_directdq_s4096_kv1024_topk512_h64_d512_direct_b16_thr256_synthetic_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_nodkv_directdq_s4096_kv1024_topk512_h64_d512_direct_b16_thr256_synthetic_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_push_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_push_decision_20260604.json) keep the TileLang branch alive. A local `no_dkv_directdq` variant removes dKV contribution/writeback and stores dQ directly. Direct `H64/D512` with `block_size=32` still misses the shared-memory limit by only `4 KiB` (`167,936` vs `163,840` bytes), but `block_size=16,threads=256` compiles and runs the full-shape non-dKV backward body at `2.19 ms`. Read: TileLang itself is viable for the full-shape QK/softmax-backward/dQ path; the next TileLang kernel should start from this direct full-head schedule and replace the per-selected dKV `T.atomic_addx4` path with a shared-memory-fitting segmented/grouped dKV reducer.
- TileLang dKV contribution/no-write gate: [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_dkv_compute_nowrite_s4096_kv1024_topk512_h64_d512_direct_b16_thr256_timing20_synthetic_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_dkv_compute_nowrite_s4096_kv1024_topk512_h64_d512_direct_b16_thr256_timing20_synthetic_20260604.json) and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_dkv_compute_nowrite_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_dkv_compute_nowrite_decision_20260604.json) restore the two TileLang dKV contribution GEMMs while still skipping global dKV writes. At the full `S4096/H64/D512/topk512` shape, `block_size=16,threads=256` runs in `2.274 ms` median over 20 timings, only `0.087 ms` slower than the no-dKV diagnostic and far below the `28.09 ms` straight atomic reference. Decision: the TileLang producer math is not the wall; the real rewrite is the compressed-group write path. A same-token-only reducer is not enough because the current CTA owns one token, so the next speed candidate must either make the producer own a token window with tile-local segmented accumulation by compressed group, or emit compact keyed partial rows for a small final reducer. The first promotion gate remains beating the `8.01 ms` current Triton sparse-atomic dKV wall.
- TileLang raw dKV overwrite gate: [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_dkv_overwrite_s4096_kv1024_topk512_h64_d512_direct_b16_thr256_timing20_synthetic_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_dkv_overwrite_s4096_kv1024_topk512_h64_d512_direct_b16_thr256_timing20_synthetic_20260604.json) and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_dkv_overwrite_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_mqa_bwd_dkv_overwrite_decision_20260604.json) add the next diagnostic split: compute the same dKV contribution GEMMs, then issue raw racy stores to `dKV[group, d]` instead of atomics. The final dKV tensor is intentionally incorrect and TileLang warns about the data race, but timing is useful. Median core time jumps from `2.274 ms` no-write to `9.259 ms` with raw stores, already slower than the current `8.01 ms` Triton sparse-atomic wall. Decision: raw selected-row global write volume is itself enough to lose; atomics explain why the straight reference is much worse, but replacing atomics with normal stores is not a speed path. The next kernel must reduce by compressed group before global memory, not emit one selected `KxD` row per token/slot as either atomics or compact partials.
- TileLang compact partial producer gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_zero_s4096_k512_tb32_sw512_d32_clustered_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_zero_s4096_k512_tb32_sw512_d32_clustered_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_static_slot_s32_k32_tb8_sw32_d32_smoke_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_static_slot_s32_k32_tb8_sw32_d32_smoke_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_static_slot_s128_k128_tb16_sw128_d32_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_static_slot_s128_k128_tb16_sw128_d32_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_decision_20260604.json) push the TileLang branch beyond raw stores. The target-shape compact output surface lowers and is cheap: S4096/topk512 clustered route has `97,541` active partial rows, `21.5x` modeled row reduction, a `190.5 MiB` FP32 partial workspace, and `0.386 ms` median zero-write timing. A constrained slot-aligned scalar math kernel also compiles and matches PyTorch (`S32` max diff `5.84e-5`, `8.18 ms`; `S128/topk128` max diff `8.71e-5`, `65.07 ms`). Decision: this is real TileLang kernel progress but not a speed candidate yet. Dynamic routed `PairSlots[token, selected]` updates and dynamic shared local tables both fail TileLang layout inference with `no available layout found`, and the intended MFMA reduced variant still fails layout lowering (`K16/D16` divide-by-zero; `K32/D32` and `K32/D64` no available layout). Keep the compact-output/static-slot harness, but production work must solve dynamic slot + MFMA lowering or move this compact producer to HIP/CK/rocWMMA.
- TileLang dynamic-slot mutable gate: [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_dynamic_slot_mutable_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_dynamic_slot_mutable_decision_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_padded_slot3_vec_atomicx4_mutable_s32_k32_tb1_sw32_d32_clustered_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_padded_slot3_vec_atomicx4_mutable_s32_k32_tb1_sw32_d32_clustered_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_padded_slot3_vec_atomicx4_mutable_s128_k128_tb1_sw128_d32_clustered_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_padded_slot3_vec_atomicx4_mutable_s128_k128_tb1_sw128_d32_clustered_20260604.json) isolate the failure more sharply. A new `padded_slot3_vec_atomicx4_mutable` mode mirrors the vendored sparse-MQA dKV write contract: caller-owned mutable partial workspace, `[route_tile, dynamic_slot, D]` output layout, selected-row `T.Parallel` lane, shared-memory source, and `T.atomic_addx4`. This compiles and passes parity when `token_block=1` (`S32/topk32` median `0.132 ms`, max diff `2.28e-5`; `S128/topk128` median `0.922 ms`, max diff `2.66e-5`). But `token_block=2/4/8` fails TileLang LayoutInference with `no available layout found`, so the working path has `1.0x` write reduction and would scale like raw selected-row emission (`~4 GiB` FP32 partials and roughly `118 ms` by simple assignment scaling at S4096/topk512). Decision: TileLang can host the per-token vendored dynamic-index pattern, but not yet the token-window segmented accumulation needed for the `~23.8x` compressed-group write reduction; continue only if TileLang lowering is fixed, otherwise implement the real producer in HIP/CK/rocWMMA.
- TileLang prepacked compact-row producer gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s128_k128_tb32_sw128_rb8_d32_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s128_k128_tb32_sw128_rb8_d32_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s512_k512_tb32_sw512_rb8_d32_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s512_k512_tb32_sw512_rb8_d32_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s4096_k512_tb32_sw512_rb8_d32_timing_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s4096_k512_tb32_sw512_rb8_d32_timing_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_prepacked_scalar_reduced_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_prepacked_scalar_reduced_decision_20260604.json) push TileLang with the prepacked route instead of dynamic output slots. The new `prepacked_scalar_reduced` mode owns compact active compressed-group rows, consumes prepacked `(token, selected)` pair lists, writes compact rows without final atomics, and passes S128 parity (`max diff 6.71e-5`). Row-blocking moves S128 from `16.95 ms` at `row_block=1` to `5.59 ms` at `row_block=8`, but topk512 scaling rejects this as the speed path: S512 is `67.51 ms` and S4096 is `562.12 ms` despite `~21.5x` write reduction and a compact `190.5 MiB` FP32 output instead of `4 GiB` selected-row writes. Decision: this proves TileLang can consume the prepacked compact-row contract, but group-owned scalar contribution production gives up query-major q/dO reuse. The next concrete kernel must keep the fast query-major contribution loop and add lane/warp/block segmented accumulation before global writes.
- TileLang route-MFMA continuation gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s16_sw64_d16_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s16_sw64_d16_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s128_tb32_sw512_d16_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s128_tb32_sw512_d16_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s4096_tb32_sw512_d32_timing_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_prepacked_scalar_reduced_s4096_tb32_sw512_d32_timing_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_route_mfma_reduced_s16_slot_aligned_sw64_d32_clearcopy_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_route_mfma_reduced_s16_slot_aligned_sw64_d32_clearcopy_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_sink_s4096_layer2_sc32_sb128_d16h64k64_timing_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_micro_sink_s4096_layer2_sc32_sb128_d16h64k64_timing_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_route_mfma_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_route_mfma_decision_20260604.json) add two concrete follow-ups. `prepacked_scalar_reduced` is correct at S16 (`max diff 4.37e-5`) but rejects itself at target shape: S4096 is `994.51 ms` plus `6.20 s` CPU prepack in this synthetic route. `route_mfma_reduced` now lowers and runs with a static `row_block=16` compact-row block, but its current output is NaN even on slot-aligned S16 after switching to the vendored `FullCol` GEMM policy and fragment-to-shared staging. The new actual-LI `dot_k_compact_micro_sink` Triton diagnostic writes only one sink vector per micro tile yet still measures `8.38 ms` at S4096, so removing selected-row writes alone is not enough for this producer. Decision: keep the correct prepacked scalar path only as a TileLang lowering baseline; the next speed branch must first make the vendored-layout TileLang MFMA contribution sink finite, then reintroduce static route-block segmented reduction.
- TileLang K64/window64 MFMA gate: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_mfma_k64_window64_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_mfma_k64_window64_decision_20260604.json) updates the route-MFMA branch with a working MI350 shape. `mfma_contrib_sink` is finite and correct with `block_k=64`, `block_d=32`, `selected_window=64`: S16 max diff `1.79e-7`, S128 max diff `2.98e-7`, and S4096 timing-only median `13.28 ms` for the contribution sink. The real `route_mfma_reduced` compact row-block reducer is also correct at S16 (`0.332 ms`, max diff `5.59e-9`) and S128 (`16.35 ms`, max diff `3.73e-9`). Decision: this is real TileLang kernel progress, but not a speed promotion. Full `selected_window=512` still NaNs, direct fragment reduction does not lower, the full active-group table stops lowering above about `64` active groups, and the row-block reducer recomputes MFMA per active-row block. The next kernel should keep the K64 MFMA body but use a bounded active-table/warp-segmented reducer that does not recompute contribution math for each group block; HIP/rocWMMA or CK may be needed if TileLang cannot express that layout.
- TileLang panelized K64 route gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `--route-pattern panel_padded_random` plus `--valid-topk`, and [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_panelized_k64_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_panelized_k64_decision_20260604.json) closes the tempting "force the route into 64-group panels" branch. The ideal slot-aligned panel route is correct at S128 (`0.406 ms`, max diff `1.30e-8`) and lowerable at S4096, but its best target timing is still only `11.78 ms` (`token_block=16`, `threads=256`) versus the retained `8.0-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic wall. The more DSv4-like padded random route, which packs 512 real selections into 1024 K64 panel slots, is correct at S128 (`0.764 ms`, max diff `7.45e-9`) but reaches `23.72 ms` at S4096. Decision: keep panelized K64 as a correctness/layout contract probe, not a latency path. Do not pad random LI routes into all group panels for production; the next branch needs true sparse segmented reduction inside the fast query-major producer, or a HIP/rocWMMA/CK kernel with explicit LDS/warp segmented control.
- TileLang panel-capacity MFMA reducer update: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `--route-pattern panel_capacity_random`, `--group-panel-size`, and overflow accounting so the route can own bounded compressed-group panels without padding every group slot. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_panel_capacity_mfma_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_panel_capacity_mfma_decision_20260604.json) retains the concrete MI350 candidate `group_panel_size=128`, `panel_capacity=96`, `topk workspace=768`, `token_block=32`, `block_k=32`, `block_d=64`, `threads=256`: S128 parity passes, S4096 has zero route overflow, and timing improves to `11.60 ms` from the previous `23.48 ms` K64 panel-padded route and `19.65 ms` full-capacity 128-panel route. This is real TileLang pre-global dKV reduction progress, but it is still above the retained `8.0-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic wall and still reads diagnostic materialized `probs/grad_logits`; next work is fusing LI derivative/prob production into this producer and cutting or eliminating the remaining `256 MiB` compact partial stream.
- TileLang compact-final atomic follow-up: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now also adds `--math-mode mfma_panel_atomic_final`, which keeps the same query-major MFMA body and in-CTA compact group reducer but atomic-adds reduced compact rows directly into final `[groups, D]` dKV. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_panel_atomic_final_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_panel_atomic_final_decision_20260604.json) shows S128 final-dKV correctness passes (`max diff 1.30e-8`) and S4096 final-atomic timing is `11.74 ms` for `token_block=32` or `11.72 ms` for `token_block=64`. This removes the `128-256 MiB` compact partial workspace and writes only a `2 MiB` final dKV, but it is slightly slower than the retained `11.60 ms` compact-partial producer, so treat it as a memory/integration branch rather than a latency promotion. The active latency wall is now contribution/body plus local accumulation, not just final partial-row HBM traffic.
- TileLang wide-panel reducer follow-up: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_panel_capacity_wide_panel_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_panel_capacity_wide_panel_decision_20260604.json) promotes a better concrete compact-partial producer shape: `group_panel_size=256`, `panel_capacity=160`, `topk workspace=640`, `token_block=32`, `block_k=32`, `block_d=64`. S128 parity passes (`max diff 9.31e-9`), S4096 has zero route overflow, and S4096 timing improves to `10.71 ms`, a `1.08x` speedup over the previous `11.60 ms` TileLang panel-capacity candidate. The same shape as direct final-dKV atomics is correct but slower at `11.47 ms`; `cap192/k64` is also correct but slower at `11.19 ms`; `block_d=128` is rejected by shared-memory pressure (`172032 > 163840`). Retain `gps256/cap160/k32/d64` as the current TileLang latency branch, while noting it is still above the `8.0-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic wall and still needs LI derivative/prob fusion plus a better way to avoid or reduce the remaining `256 MiB` compact partial stream.
- TileLang actual-LI selected-limit promotion: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `--math-mode mfma_panel_atomic_final_limited` plus per-route selected-limit metadata for real `actual_li_panel` routes. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_actual_li_selected_limit_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_actual_li_selected_limit_decision_20260604.json) promotes this as the current actual-route TileLang compressed-dKV candidate. The kernel keeps the query-major panel MFMA contribution body and final `[groups, D]` atomic-add contract, but skips `block_k` chunks that are padded-empty for the whole token/panel route tile. S512 correctness passes with max diff `3.73e-8`. On the hard S4096 layer-2 LI route, the best sweep point is `token_block=16`, `cap512`, `K64/D64`, `threads=512`: `6.913 ms`, route-limit modeled chunk fraction `0.431`, and a `1.84x` speedup over the prior actual-route `12.735 ms` panel-final baseline. It now beats the retained `8.0-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic dKV wall, so the next work is semantic integration and fusion: feed/fuse LI target-prob and derivative production, connect the compressor/LI dKV consumer, and keep the no-selected-state saved-tensor contract.
- TileLang actual-boundary input validation: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `--actual-li-input-source boundary`, which keeps the real LI route capture but also feeds real TorchTitan sparse-MLA boundary `q`, `dO`, per-head `probs`, and scaled `grad_logits` into the selected-limit TileLang producer. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_actual_li_boundary_inputs_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_actual_li_boundary_inputs_decision_20260604.json) validates the promoted candidate against real tensor values: S512 correctness passes with max diff `9.54e-6`, and S4096 layer-2 timing is `6.910 ms`, effectively identical to the random-input selected-limit run (`6.913 ms`) while still `1.84x` faster than the prior actual-route panel-final baseline. This de-risks the kernel result as not merely a random-weight artifact. Caveat: the boundary-input run still materializes S4096 per-head `probs` and `grad_logits` outside the timed producer (`512 MiB` each), so the next production step is fusing/recomputing those tensors inside or adjacent to the TileLang producer and then connecting final dKV to the compressor/LI backward consumer.
- TileLang TorchTitan selected-limit compressed-dKV bridge gate (historical control): [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/verify_torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_backward_bridge.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/verify_torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_backward_bridge.py) originally wired the selected-limit TileLang producer into `sparse_mla_shared_kv` backward; that route-plan path is now retained as the `TORCHTITAN_DSV4_SPARSE_MLA_SHAREDKV_BACKWARD_MODE=tilelang_materialized_dkv` control, while `explicit_tilelang_dkv` uses the plan-free group-filter update below. The bridge keeps explicit PyTorch dQ/local-dKV/sink math as the oracle path, then replaces only the compressed dKV slice with TileLang final `[groups,D]` output. The important invariant is that LI top-k groups are unique per token; a with-replacement synthetic route falsely failed the compact reducer. With unique LI-style routes, S128/H64/D512/K128 default `tb16` matches the TileLang BF16 panel oracle within `0.0039` and explicit PyTorch within `0.03125` max dKV diff in [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_s128_h64_d512_k128_unique_tb16_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_s128_h64_d512_k128_unique_tb16_20260604.json). The adapter now uses vectorized panel packing plus a dense route-tile/group-panel slot map: S512/H64/D512/local128/K128 bridge timing drops from the original `581 ms` to `9.20 ms` while preserving compressed-dKV parity (`0.00098` max diff versus the TileLang BF16 panel oracle, `0.03125` versus explicit PyTorch) in [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_s512_h64_d512_k128_unique_tb128_fastplan2_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_s512_h64_d512_k128_unique_tb128_fastplan2_20260604.json). The S4096/H64/D512/local128+compressed512 timing-only bridge is now `75.75 ms` in [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_s4096_h64_d512_k512_unique_tb16_timing_fastplan2_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_s4096_h64_d512_k512_unique_tb16_timing_fastplan2_20260604.json). Caveat: this historical selected-limit bridge is still not a production speed path; it still materializes selected-KV/probs/grad_logits and still builds route metadata on CPU. The remaining production work is GPU/reused LI route packing plus fused or adjacent P/dP production so the `6.18-6.91 ms` kernel-only candidate can matter inside TorchTitan.
- TileLang selected-limit adapter/native-layout update: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/tilelang_sparse_dkv_selected_limit_adapter.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/tilelang_sparse_dkv_selected_limit_adapter.py), [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_selected_limit_adapter.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_selected_limit_adapter.py), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_adapter_bshd_s512_correct_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_adapter_bshd_s512_correct_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_adapter_bshd_s4096_tb16_cap512_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_adapter_bshd_s4096_tb16_cap512_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_selected_limit_adapter_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_selected_limit_adapter_decision_20260604.json) move the promoted kernel out of CLI-only status. The adapter separates static LI route planning, dynamic materialized-weight packing, and the TileLang final-dKV launch. It also adds a native `[S,H,D]` input-layout kernel so TorchTitan-shaped `q/dO` no longer need a `[S,D,H]` copy before launch. S512 correctness still passes (`9.54e-6` max diff). At S4096 layer 2, native-layout kernel-only timing is `6.180 ms`, `1.12x` faster than the previous `[S,D,H]` CLI kernel (`6.910 ms`) and `1.26x` faster than the adapter path that included layout conversion (`7.650 ms`). The fast-plan rerun [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_adapter_bshd_s4096_tb16_cap512_fastplan2_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_adapter_bshd_s4096_tb16_cap512_fastplan2_20260604.json) keeps kernel-only at `6.23 ms` and pack+kernel at `8.81 ms`, while reducing static route-plan wall from `6702 ms` to `563 ms`. Decision: promote the native-layout TileLang dKV kernel candidate; do not promote the materialized packing bridge as production. The next step is eliminating CPU route-plan work and materialized P/dP slabs by reusing/GPU-producing LI route metadata and consuming probability/LI derivative tensors inside or adjacent to the dKV producer.
- TileLang plan-free group-filter dKV update: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/tilelang_sparse_dkv_selected_limit_adapter.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/tilelang_sparse_dkv_selected_limit_adapter.py), [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/verify_torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_backward_bridge.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/verify_torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_backward_bridge.py), and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_group_filter_dkv_bridge_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_group_filter_dkv_bridge_decision_20260604.json) add a real plan-free TileLang compressed-dKV kernel. It consumes original `[S,K,H]` probabilities/logit derivatives plus the original `[S,K]` compressed-group route, filters by group panel inside the TileLang CTA, reduces into a group-panel accumulator, and atomically writes final `[groups,D]` dKV without CPU panel packing. S128/S512 parity matches the packed selected-limit path exactly in [`run_artifacts/tilelang_group_filter_adapter_s128_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_group_filter_adapter_s128_20260604.json) and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_group_filter_adapter_s512_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_group_filter_adapter_s512_20260604.json). At S4096, the best plan-free shape so far is `group_panel_size=256`, `block_d=64`: dKV kernel median `12.12 ms` in [`run_artifacts/tilelang_group_filter_adapter_s4096_gp256_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_group_filter_adapter_s4096_gp256_20260604.json). The TorchTitan bridge improves from the old selected-limit `~72-75 ms` GPU event to `32.05 ms` GPU event / `32.11 ms` wall in [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_group_filter_s4096_timing_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_group_filter_s4096_timing_20260604.json), but the same-shape explicit PyTorch bridge is still slightly faster at `31.00 ms` GPU event / `31.05 ms` wall in [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_group_filter_s4096_vs_pytorch_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_group_filter_s4096_vs_pytorch_20260604.json). Decision: keep `explicit_pytorch` as the stable default, keep `explicit_tilelang_dkv` as the plan-free TileLang candidate gate, and return to selected-limit scheduling only when LI route metadata is already available on device or fused into the producer.

S512 selected-limit-source parity is clean in the expected BF16 band (`0.015625` max diff versus the TileLang BF16 compressed-dKV reference, `0.03125` versus explicit PyTorch) in [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_selected_limit_source_s512_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge_selected_limit_source_s512_20260604.json). Decision: promote the selected-limit TileLang body as the higher-return S4096 dKV branch, but do not promote the bridge as production until LI route metadata is reused/GPU-produced and P/scaled-dP are fused or adjacent-produced without selected-state slabs.
- TileLang selected-limit source actual-LI rerun: [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_source_actual_li_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_source_actual_li_decision_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_source_actual_li_s128_layer2_gp32_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_source_actual_li_s128_layer2_gp32_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_source_actual_li_s4096_layer2_gp512_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_source_actual_li_s4096_layer2_gp512_20260604.json) pin the concrete kernel after the raw-overwrite diagnostic. - TileLang selected-limit grouped-D/panel sweep: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/tilelang_sparse_dkv_selected_limit_adapter.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/tilelang_sparse_dkv_selected_limit_adapter.py), [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_selected_limit_adapter.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_selected_limit_adapter.py), and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_grouped_d_and_panel_sweep_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_grouped_d_and_panel_sweep_decision_20260604.json) add and close a concrete follow-up kernel branch. The new `--d-blocks-per-kernel` grouped-D TileLang variant produces real final `[groups,D]` dKV and passes S128 correctness (`6.68e-6` max diff), but the useful S4096 `D64x2` shape exceeds MI350 shared memory (`294912` requested vs `163840` bytes), and the legal `D32x2` shape regresses to `7.25 ms` packed / `8.13 ms` source-indexed. A smaller `gp256/cap256` panel also regresses (`6.76 ms` packed / `7.64 ms` source), while `gp1024/cap512` fails TileLang layout inference. Decision: retain `gp512/cap512/K64/D64/dblocks1` as the best TileLang selected-limit dKV body and stop pursuing full `max_active_groups x D` grouped-D accumulators; the next branch needs a smaller keyed/segmented in-producer reducer or lower-level HIP/CK/rocWMMA control.
