- Tile-segment D-block head-split reducer gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator.py), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_dblock_headsplit_s128_layer2_t32k256_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_dblock_headsplit_s128_layer2_t32k256_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_dblock_headsplit_s512_layer2_t32k256_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_dblock_headsplit_s512_layer2_t32k256_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_dblock_headsplit_s4096_layer2_t32k512_timing_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_dblock_headsplit_s4096_layer2_t32k512_timing_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/tile_segment_dblock_headsplit_reducer_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tile_segment_dblock_headsplit_reducer_decision_20260604.json) close the obvious smaller segmented-reducer follow-up outside TileLang. The new HIP kernel owns one prepacked tile-local compressed-group segment and one D block, splits H64 across lanes, reduces in shared memory, then emits one reduced compressed-dKV row slice. S128/S512 correctness passes (`1.91e-5` / `3.43e-5` max diff), and S512 timing is acceptable at `1.38 ms`, but S4096 fails badly: D16 is `117.53 ms` and D64 sanity is `84.50 ms` versus the `8.806 ms` sparse-atomic wall and retained TileLang selected-limit `~6.18 ms` packed body. Decision: do not pursue scalar segment-owned D-block reducers as the speed path; keep the TileLang selected-limit MFMA body and focus the next concrete work on removing materialized `P`/scaled-`dP` slabs plus source-route bridge overhead.
- TileLang selected-limit route-plan timing: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/tilelang_sparse_dkv_selected_limit_adapter.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/tilelang_sparse_dkv_selected_limit_adapter.py) now has an opt-in `TILELANG_SELECTED_LIMIT_DIRECT_PLAN=1` direct device planner, and [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_selected_limit_adapter.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_selected_limit_adapter.py) records warmed route-plan timing. [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_plan_timing_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_plan_timing_decision_20260604.json) rejects the direct planner as a speed path: it is correct at S128, but S4096 warmed plan timing is `10.11 ms` versus the retained legacy planner's `1.55 ms`. The old `~180 ms` static plan wall is a cold-start artifact, not the steady-state route cost. Decision: keep legacy selected-limit planning as the default (`TILELANG_SELECTED_LIMIT_DIRECT_PLAN=0`) and focus the next sparse-dKV work on eliminating materialized P/scaled-dP slabs and their `~2.0 ms` pack path.
- TileLang selected-limit bridge stage profile: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/profile_torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/profile_torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge.py) now supports `--plan-on-device` and optional packed-control timing so it can match the `selected_limit_source` bridge path. [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_source_bridge_stage_profile_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_source_bridge_stage_profile_decision_20260604.json) records the S4096 verifier-route decomposition: autograd bridge timing is `30.13 ms`, manual component median sum is `31.60 ms`, and the largest stages are source-indexed TileLang compressed dKV (`9.81 ms`), selected-KV gather (`3.24 ms`), QK scores (`2.49 ms`), `dO.V` grad-probs (`2.30 ms`), dQ (`2.30 ms`), local scatter (`2.09 ms`), forward-with-LSE (`1.92 ms`), and route plan (`1.73 ms`). Caveat: this profile uses the verifier's synthetic unique compressed route, not actual LI layer-2 fan-in; it has `2.10M` valid compressed pairs and `8.0x` write reduction versus the actual-LI layer-2 adapter reference of `1.57M` pairs and `11.95x`. Decision: device-side selected-limit planning is no longer the lead wall in this bridge profile; the next production work is actual-LI stage profiling plus fusing/removing selected-KV/P/dP materialization and keeping the selected-limit dKV body.
- TileLang selected-limit actual-LI bridge stage profile: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/profile_torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/profile_torchtitan_shared_kv_tilelang_bridge.py) now adds `--input-source actual-li-boundary`, which captures real TorchTitan layer-2 LI routing/tensors and profiles the compressed branch with `local_count=0`. [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_actual_li_bridge_stage_profile_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_actual_li_bridge_stage_profile_decision_20260604.json), [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_actual_li_bridge_stage_profile_s128_layer2_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_actual_li_bridge_stage_profile_s128_layer2_20260604.json), and [`run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_actual_li_bridge_stage_profile_s4096_layer2_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/tilelang_selected_limit_actual_li_bridge_stage_profile_s4096_layer2_20260604.json) remove the synthetic-route caveat. At S4096/H64/D512/topk512, the actual LI route has `1,572,352` valid pairs and `11.95x` write reduction. The source-indexed TileLang compressed-dKV body is `7.31 ms`; the materialized bridge component median sum is `21.47 ms`, led by dKV `7.31 ms`, selected-KV gather `2.47 ms`, route plan `1.76 ms`, dQ `1.69 ms`, `dO.V` `1.68 ms`, QK scores `1.63 ms`, and forward/LSE `1.44 ms`. Decision: promote the actual-LI profile mode and keep the selected-limit dKV body, but do not promote the materialized bridge; the next kernel work is fusing or adjacent-producing QK/softmax row terms/`dO.V`/grad-logits/dQ/compressed dKV without selected-KV, probability, or grad-logit slabs.
- TileLang slab-free recompute gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `--math-mode mfma_panel_atomic_final_recompute_limited`, which consumes real boundary `q/dO/output/lse/compressed_kv` plus packed group ids and recomputes sparse-MLA probabilities and scaled grad-logits inside the TileLang producer instead of reading materialized `[S, topk, H]` slabs. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_recompute_limited_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_recompute_limited_decision_20260604.json) validates the contract but rejects it as a speed candidate: S128/S512 correctness against the materialized oracle is in the BF16 recompute band (`~1.5e-2` max diff), S4096 timing-only runs avoid the two `512 MiB` probability/grad-logit tensors, and the best no-overflow target-shape point is `89.07 ms` (`group_panel_size=128`, `selected_window=128`, `block_d=64`). That is `12.89x` slower than the retained materialized-input selected-limit producer (`6.910 ms`) because the all-in-one D-block-owned schedule recomputes full-D QK and `dO.KV` for every output D block. Decision: retain this as a fused-contract correctness gate only; the next TileLang rewrite must compute probability/grad-logit tiles once per token/selected tile and reuse them across D-block dKV accumulation.
- TileLang P/dP recompute-once gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `--math-mode recompute_pdp_sink_limited`, a concrete TileLang kernel that consumes real boundary `q/dO/output/lse/compressed_kv` plus selected-limit route metadata, recomputes sparse probabilities and scaled dP once per token/selected tile, and writes only a tiny `[route_tiles, H]` checksum sink. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_recompute_pdp_sink_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_recompute_pdp_sink_decision_20260604.json) shows S128/S512 correctness against the materialized oracle passes in the expected BF16 recompute band (`7.74e-3` max diff), and S4096 timing improves dramatically versus all-in-one recompute: best K128 is `8.423 ms` versus `89.07 ms`. But this is still already the current sparse-atomic dKV wall before doing any dKV accumulation or writeback; K64 is `9.380 ms`, K256 regresses to `11.611 ms`, and `token_block=32` regresses to `14.103 ms` despite better modeled write reduction. Decision: keep this as a useful TileLang row-term gate, but do not build the production path as a detached P/dP recompute stage; fuse P/dP production exactly where the selected-limit dKV producer consumes it, or move the fused segmented producer to HIP/CK/rocWMMA if TileLang cannot express that reuse.
- TileLang adjacent P/dP slab-producer gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `--math-mode recompute_pdp_store_limited`, which recomputes the same P and scaled-dP tiles from real boundary tensors and writes them as one packed BF16 `[2, S, topk, H]` slab. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_recompute_pdp_store_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_recompute_pdp_store_decision_20260604.json) closes the tempting two-kernel adjacent path. S128 parity is clean (`1.95e-3` max diff); S512 is timing-useful but not promotion-quality numerically yet (`0.367` max diff, tiny mean diff). The S4096 target-shape slab producer is `8.689 ms` with `5.13 GiB` peak, only slightly slower than checksum-only K128 (`8.423 ms`), so full-slab HBM writes are not the main cost. But slab producer plus the existing selected-limit dKV consumer projects to `15.599 ms` before integration overhead (`8.689 + 6.910`), so production must not be `P/dP producer -> materialized slabs -> dKV consumer`. The next speed branch remains true on-chip P/dP consumption inside the selected-limit dKV producer, or a HIP/CK/rocWMMA fused segmented producer if TileLang cannot express that schedule.
- TileLang concrete P/dP+dKV follow-up: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds two real TileLang follow-up modes, `recompute_pdp_store_then_dkv_limited` and `recompute_pdp_grouped_dkv_limited`, summarized in [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_pdp_pipeline_grouped_dkv_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_pdp_pipeline_grouped_dkv_decision_20260604.json). The measured two-kernel slab pipeline confirms the projected rejection: the full no-overflow S4096 actual route (`topk=1024` padded panel carrying `actual_li_topk=512`, cap512, K64/D64) is `16.238 ms`, slower than the `8.0-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic wall. The explicit `topk=512` split-panel timing is `12.868 ms`, but it drops `333843` overflow pairs because recompute spill is not implemented, so it is a fit check, not a full-route result. The grouped-D fused mode keeps P/dP on chip and passes S128/S512 with BF16-band diffs (`~1.5e-2` max) at `1.928/3.382 ms`, but useful S4096 reuse shapes exceed MI350 shared memory (`290-303 KiB` requested vs `160 KiB` limit), and the only legal S4096 shape tried (`D32x2`) is `61.642 ms`. Decision: keep the TileLang source prototypes, but do not promote either branch; the next kernel must use a smaller keyed/segmented in-producer reducer instead of a full `max_active_groups x D` accumulator or a materialized P/dP slab.
- TileLang recompute spill-overflow gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now lets final-dKV modes use `--spill-overflow` and wires the existing panel-MFMA spill kernel into `recompute_pdp_store_then_dkv_limited`, recorded in [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_recompute_spill_overflow_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_recompute_spill_overflow_decision_20260604.json). This closes the prior incomplete-route caveat: S512 overflow correctness passes in BF16 recompute band (`0.0145` max diff) while adding `12224` overflow pairs. But the S4096 `topk=512/gp512/cap256` split-panel route becomes `19.848 ms` once its `333843` overflow pairs are included, with spill-only at `6.973 ms` and `3.13 GiB` peak. Decision: capacity-limited panels plus a separate spill kernel are not a speed path; only fused overflow handling or a true sparse segmented producer should revisit this branch.
- TileLang chunked grouped recompute gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `recompute_pdp_chunked_grouped_dkv_limited` plus chunk-level active-group metadata and a compile-safe `recompute_pdp_chunked_rowblock_dkv_limited` fallback, summarized in [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_chunked_grouped_recompute_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_chunked_grouped_recompute_decision_20260604.json). S512 correctness passes in BF16 recompute band (`0.0145` max diff) and runs at `2.784 ms`. At S4096, `gp512/cap512` full chunks fail TileLang layout, row-block fallback compiles but is `1596.6 ms`, and the best legal full-route grouped shape is `gp128/cap128 K64 D32x8` at `42.85 ms`, improving the old legal grouped-D point (`61.64 ms`) but still `6.2x` slower than the materialized-input selected-limit dKV producer (`6.91 ms`). Decision: keep the materialized-input selected-limit TileLang producer as the current dKV output candidate; slab-free fused P/dP+dKV needs a lower-level HIP/CK/rocWMMA reducer or a stronger TileLang grouped-accumulator primitive.
- TileLang final-output fold check: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `--fold-final-dkv`, which keeps the current compact-partial producer and folds compact rows into final `[groups, D]` dKV with a measured PyTorch `index_add_` diagnostic. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_fold_final_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_fold_final_decision_20260604.json) shows S128 final-dKV parity passes (`max diff 1.49e-8`), S4096 compact producer plus final fold is `10.956 ms`, and fold-only is only `0.229 ms`. This beats the same-shape direct reduced-atomic final-output branch (`11.473 ms`) by `0.517 ms`, so the retained full-output TileLang branch is compact producer plus final fold, not reduced final atomics. The follow-up read-elision diagnostic below shows LI/probability fusion alone is not the missing speed lever; producer topology and launch shape are.
- TileLang materialized-weight read-elision diagnostic: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `--weight-source constant`, which fills the P/dP shared tiles from constants instead of reading materialized `[S, topk, H]` probability and grad-logit tensors. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_constant_weight_read_elision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_constant_weight_read_elision_20260604.json) shows S128 final-dKV parity passes and S4096 full-output is effectively unchanged: `10.959 ms` constant versus `10.956 ms` input, with fold-only `0.228 ms`. Decision: eliding those HBM reads does not move the wall. LI/probability fusion remains important for memory and semantic integration, but the speed branch has to change the producer/reducer shape.
- TileLang wide-panel/512-thread speed branch: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_wide_panel_thr512_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_wide_panel_thr512_decision_20260604.json) promotes the current concrete TileLang dKV candidate: `token_block=64`, `group_panel_size=512`, `panel_capacity=320`, `topk workspace=640`, `block_k=64`, `block_d=64`, `threads=512`, `--fold-final-dkv`. S128 final-dKV parity passes (`max diff 1.49e-8`), S4096 has zero route overflow, full final-dKV output is `8.204 ms`, and fold-only is `0.119 ms`. This is a `1.34x` speedup over the previous retained full-output TileLang branch (`10.956 ms`) and lands in the same band as the `8.0-8.8 ms` Triton sparse-atomic wall while preserving the reduced-row final-output contract. The active next step is a proper small final reducer or direct compressor-dKV consumer, then LI/probability fusion for memory/correctness.
- TileLang direct final-atomic comparison: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_final_atomic_vs_fold_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_final_atomic_vs_fold_decision_20260604.json) tests the same wide-panel shape with `--math-mode mfma_panel_atomic_final`, which atomically adds reduced compact rows directly into final `[groups, D]` dKV and removes the `128 MiB` compact partial stream. S128 final-dKV parity passes, but S4096 target timing is `8.787 ms`, slower than the retained compact-partial plus fold path at `8.204 ms`; `threads=1024` on the fold path is also slower at `8.358 ms`. Decision: retain `tb64/gps512/cap320/k64/d64/threads512` compact partials plus a small final reducer for latency. Direct final atomics are only a lower-workspace integration branch if the partial workspace becomes the bottleneck.
- TileLang panel-dense final fold: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now adds `--fold-backend tilelang_panel_dense`, a no-atomic TileLang final reducer for the dense `panel_capacity_random` compact-row layout. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_panel_dense_fold_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_panel_dense_fold_decision_20260604.json) shows S128 final-dKV parity still passes (`max diff 1.49e-8`), S4096 full final-dKV output improves slightly to `8.130 ms`, and fold-only drops from `0.119 ms` PyTorch `index_add_` to `0.0485 ms`. This is a real TileLang final-output contract, but the full-path improvement is only `0.074 ms`, so the remaining wall is the query-major compact producer and its `128 MiB` partial stream, not the final fold.
- TileLang token-window producer sweep: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_token_block_sweep_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_token_block_sweep_decision_20260604.json) sweeps the retained `gps512/cap320/k64/d64/threads512` panel-dense final-output branch over `token_block=64/128/192/256/512`. The new retained point is `token_block=256`: S128 final-dKV parity passes (`max diff 1.86e-8`), S4096 full final-dKV output is `7.990 ms`, fold-only is `0.014 ms`, and the compact partial stream shrinks to `32 MiB` with `128x` modeled write reduction. `token_block=128` is only `8.091 ms`, while non-power `192` and wider `512` regress badly to `12.025 ms` and `15.915 ms`; this is a scheduling/parallelism knee, not a monotonic memory curve. Retain `tb256/gps512/cap320/k64/d64/threads512/fold_backend=tilelang_panel_dense` as the current TileLang sparse-dKV branch.
- TileLang actual-LI route kernel gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_tilelang_sparse_dkv_compact_partial.py) now has real TorchTitan LI route capture via `--route-pattern actual_li` and `actual_li_panel`, plus `--fold-backend tilelang_panel_sparse` and `--math-mode mfma_panel_atomic_final`. [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_actual_li_route_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_actual_li_route_decision_20260604.json) records the first working actual-route TileLang branch. Small S128 actual-LI correctness passes with max diff `1.86e-8`. At S4096 layer 2, full-capacity `actual_li_panel` has no dropped route pairs and models `180.75x` compact-row reduction at `token_block=256`, but the naive sparse TileLang fold is rejected (`20.884 ms` full, `7.542 ms` fold-only). Reduced final atomics are better: `tb256` is `13.256 ms`, `tb128` is `13.065 ms`, `tb64` is `12.791 ms`, and `tb32` is the current best correct actual-route final-dKV run at `12.735 ms`. Capacity-limited panels demonstrate the speed pressure but are not correctness-preserving without a spill path: cap448 is `11.797 ms` with `1.09%` overflow, cap384 is `10.252 ms` with `4.59%` overflow, and cap320 is `8.708 ms` with `11.04%` overflow. Decision: do not promote this into TorchTitan yet; the synthetic `7.990 ms` branch remains an idealized panel route, while the real LI route needs either a correctness-preserving overflow/spill path or a truly sparse segmented producer that avoids padding every token into two 512-slot panels.
- TileLang actual-LI spill-overflow follow-up: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_actual_li_spill_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_actual_li_spill_decision_20260604.json) closes the correctness-preserving spill branch for cap-limited actual-LI panels. The new `--spill-overflow --spill-mode panel_mfma` path runs the fast cap-limited main panel, then launches a second TileLang panel-MFMA kernel over dropped overflow pairs and atomically adds them into final `[groups,D]` dKV. It is mechanically real and complete: cap448, cap384, and cap320 all have zero second-stage overflow and matching output checksum `6397.074`. But the spill removes the speed win: cap448/cap384/cap320 full medians are `14.359/14.351/14.386 ms`, with spill-only medians `2.483/4.094/5.669 ms`, all slower than the full-capacity correct actual-route `12.735 ms`. Decision: do not pursue two-kernel cap-limited spill for latency; the next actual-route TileLang step needs a true sparse segmented producer or LI/probability fusion, not padded panels plus residual spill.
- TileLang actual-LI residual-spill follow-up: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_actual_li_spill_decision_20260604.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_tilelang_actual_li_spill_decision_20260604.json) adds a correctness-preserving overflow path for capacity-limited `actual_li_panel`. The working spill mode repacks overflow pairs into residual panel slots and runs a second `mfma_panel_atomic_final` TileLang reducer; S512/cap64 correctness passes (`max diff 7.45e-8`) and spill-only improves from the scalar diagnostic's `~8.61 ms` to `2.389 ms`. At S4096, though, the split-capacity candidates lose once corrected: cap448 becomes `14.185 ms` full with `2.394 ms` spill-only, and cap384 becomes `14.360 ms` full with `4.109 ms` spill-only. A full-capacity `tb16` sweep is also slower at `12.849 ms`, so retain the prior full-capacity actual-route `tb32/cap512` final-atomic candidate at `12.735 ms`. Decision: residual-panel spill is real kernel progress but not a latency promotion; the next branch needs one-kernel fused residual handling or true sparse segmented reduction, not another detached spill pass.
- Ascend SASG ScatterAdd source mapping: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_ascend_sasg_scatteradd_source_mapping_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_ascend_sasg_scatteradd_source_mapping_20260603.json) pins the reference implementation detail behind the SASG pipeline diagram. In the extracted CANN source, `SparseAttnSharedkvGrad` runs Cube and Vector work in ping-pong order, `Cube345` writes dK/dV contribution rows into `mm4ResWorkspaceGm/mm5ResWorkspaceGm`, and `VecOp::ScatterAdd` enables `SetAtomicAdd<float>()`, reads those rows through UB in 16-row chunks, scales/adds dk+dv, resolves compressed versus original KV destination, and atomically writes to the final KV-grad workspace. So the AMD lesson is not to remove ScatterAdd semantics; it is to make the current fast query-major `dot_k_atomic` producer feed ScatterAdd fewer already-reduced rows. The promoted next rung is `query_major_segmented_scatteradd_v1`: keep the `tl.dot` query-major contribution loop, use prepacked LI route metadata for lane/warp/block segmented accumulation inside the producer, and only then emit compact partials or reduced atomics.
- Sparse dKV micro-partial runtime gate: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_dkv_micro_partial_store.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_dkv_micro_partial_store.py), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_micro_partial_store_s128_layer2_sc16_u64d16h64k32_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_micro_partial_store_s128_layer2_sc16_u64d16h64k32_20260603.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_micro_partial_store_s4096_layer2_sc32_u256d16h64k128_timing_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_micro_partial_store_s4096_layer2_sc32_u256d16h64k128_timing_20260603.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_micro_partial_store_s4096_layer2_sc32_u128d16h64k64_timing_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_micro_partial_store_s4096_layer2_sc32_u128d16h64k64_timing_20260603.json), and [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_micro_partial_store_runtime_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_micro_partial_store_runtime_decision_20260603.json) close that K-microtile branch at runtime. The new probe passes S128 parity (`max_abs_diff=0.0841`) and reproduces the modeled S4096 `K128` first-level reduction (`805M -> 126M` scalar elements, `6.37x`), but S4096 layer-2 `K128` emit-only is `58.40 ms` and emit-plus-`index_add` is `58.89 ms`; `K64` is worse at `106.85 ms`. Since the current direct sparse-atomic wall is `~8.0 ms`, the dense `active_group x selected_K` route-matrix micro producer is rejected. Next kernel should keep the query-major selected-K dot producer and cheap route metadata, but perform true sparse keyed local/segmented reduction before global writes without expanding to dense active-group route matrices.
- Sparse dKV pair-slot source diagnosis: [`run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_pairslot_local_table_source_diagnosis_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_dkv_pairslot_local_table_source_diagnosis_20260603.json) pins why the best compact pair-slot reducer is still not the missing primitive. In `probe_compressed_dkv_rocwmma_route_grid.py`, `compressed_dkv_route_grid_compact_pairslot_atomic_bf16_kernel` keeps query-major rocWMMA contribution generation and uses compact route metadata, but line-level inspection shows it still performs one `group_acc[slot, d] += contrib` local-table update per selected contribution before emitting reduced global atomics. At S4096 layer 2, `32x512` gets the modeled `23.81x` global-write reduction, but `contrib_sink` is `8.997 ms` and full pair-slot local-table accumulation is `18.447 ms` versus the retained `8.806 ms` sparse-atomic wall. Decision: do not retry dense/compact local tables; the next kernel must combine selected rows with lane/warp/block segmented reduction before they touch either global dKV or an active-group local table.
- Actual-LI hot-group hybrid reduction model: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/analyze_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_tile_coalescing.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/analyze_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_tile_coalescing.py), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_hot_group_hybrid_reduction_s4096_layer2_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_hot_group_hybrid_reduction_s4096_layer2_20260603.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_hot_group_hybrid_reduction_wide_s4096_layer2_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_hot_group_hybrid_reduction_wide_s4096_layer2_20260603.json), and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_hot_group_hybrid_reduction_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_hot_group_hybrid_reduction_decision_20260603.json) reject a small bounded top-N local accumulator as the next sparse-dKV kernel. In the primary `token_block=32`, `selected_block=512` tile, full segmented grouping models `23.81x` write reduction, but hot-256 is only `1.96x` and hot-512 is only `4.81x`; useful reduction appears only at hot-768 to hot-1024, which collapses back into the wide active-list/local-table problem already rejected by runtime probes. The next kernel should keep query-major MFMA contribution production and implement true full-tile sparse segmented/grouped accumulation across waves/CTAs before global writes, not a small top-N table plus tail atomics.
- Actual-LI prepacked panel-D16 contribution sink: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_prepacked_route_panel_d16_contrib_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_prepacked_route_panel_d16_contrib_decision_20260603.json) rejects moving the contribution producer itself to token-panel/group-panel ownership. The new `--include-panel-d16-contrib-sink` path compiles and is fine at short sequence (`S128` `0.646 ms`, `S512` best `0.863 ms`), but the hard S4096 layer-2 route is `111-130 ms` even though it only writes a checksum and never updates dKV. `panel_block_k=32/64` stays around `111/110 ms`. Decision: route prepack/traversal remains useful, but the producer must stay in the existing fast query-major dot-K/MFMA shape; the next real kernel should graft lane/warp/tile-local grouped or segmented dKV reduction onto that producer before global writes, not re-own the producer by token panel.
- The NVIDIA Day-0 RL stack reports DSv4 support across DP/TP/SP/EP/PP/CP, compressed-attention TP/SP/CP handling, mHC p2p shape changes, TileLang kernels for indexer/sparse MLA/mHC, FP8 rollout, BF16/FP8 training, FP8 attention QAT, R3, and experimental indexer replay.
- The Ascend CANN recipe reports a TorchTitan-NPU DeepSeek-V4-Flash BF16 4K target on 64 Atlas A3 cards, using pure FSDP plus large EP and CANN AutoFuse. The active experiment pass/fail target is now the `~12.2k` tok/GPU/s gate above, first on `flash_12layer_ceiling_probe`; the `~277 TFLOPs/GPU` proxy is retained as aspirational parity context.
- Backward ops shape trace: [`docs/dsv4_nvidia_backward_ops_path.md`](docs/dsv4_nvidia_backward_ops_path.md).
- Standalone single-layer microbench harness and MI350 smoke results: [`metrics.md`](metrics.md).
- Current single-layer gap after the LI retune: [`run_artifacts/single_layer_current_gap_after_li_tile_20260601.json`](run_artifacts/single_layer_current_gap_after_li_tile_20260601.json). Against the updated `24.9 ms` S4096 target, the best fixed-router packed-sim full-layer evidence is `68.21 ms` (`2.74x` target time, `36.5%` of target layer-token rate), and the learned-router bridge is `77.44 ms` (`3.11x`). The improved shared-KV attention plus unfused LI diagnostic floor is `27.85 ms` before MoE/residual/RMSNorm/full compressor integration, so the single-layer path is still not close enough for a final perf canary.
- Single-layer gap attribution ladder: [`run_artifacts/single_layer_gap_attribution_ladder_20260601.json`](run_artifacts/single_layer_gap_attribution_ladder_20260601.json), with normal-backward profiler cross-check in [`run_artifacts/single_layer_s4096_fixed_torchtrace_20260601.json`](run_artifacts/single_layer_s4096_fixed_torchtrace_20260601.json). The clean baseline still needs `43.31 ms` reduction from `68.21 ms` to `24.9 ms`. The profiler trace is slower at `71.04 ms` but confirms the shape: `24.77 ms` forward, `46.12 ms` backward, and backward kernel time dominated by Cijk/GEMM-family work (`36.17 ms`) with copy/cast movement second-order (`3.55 ms`). SGLang `run_dsv4.sh` runtime evidence in [`run_artifacts/sglang_dsv4_run_env_forward_comparability_20260601.json`](run_artifacts/sglang_dsv4_run_env_forward_comparability_20260601.json) says the current `22.58 ms` forward is a valid TorchTitan training-proxy number, but SGLang is an inference/TP8/FP8-KV fusion reference, not a direct training-latency oracle. The closure order remains fused compressed-topk sparse-MLA backward, fused LI/compressor integration, compact-native grouped MoE training GEMM/backward, then residual/RMSNorm/bookkeeping cleanup.
- Ascend SASG/SLIG to AMD fusion contract: [`run_artifacts/ascend_sasg_slig_amd_fusion_contract_20260601.json`](run_artifacts/ascend_sasg_slig_amd_fusion_contract_20260601.json). It records the Ascend `SparseAttnSharedkvGrad` five-stage Gather/Cube/Process/Cube/Scatter contract, the `SparseLightningIndexerGradKLLoss` deferred-backward contract, and the clean AMD H64/N64 query-major route-slice attribution. Full local+compressed is `14.39 ms`, local-only is `3.83 ms`, and compressed-only is `11.02 ms`, so the compressed top-k route accounts for about `76.5%` of the full raw backward slice. The follow-up structured-index probe in [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_sparse_mla_shared_kv_structured_index_route_probe_20260601.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_sparse_mla_shared_kv_structured_index_route_probe_20260601.json) shows eliminating synthetic route-index tensor loads saves only `0.03-0.06 ms`; route-index loading is not the wall. The inverse-route two-pass dKV sweep in [`run_artifacts/structured_dkv_inverse_route_sweep_20260601/summary.json`](run_artifacts/structured_dkv_inverse_route_sweep_20260601/summary.json) is also negative at S4096: the best observed structured point is `140.67 ms`, with larger-block/lower-scratch points at `432-483 ms`, versus `14.39 ms` for the retained query-major raw slice. A focused compressed-only tile sweep in [`run_artifacts/shared_kv_compressed_tile_sweep_20260601/summary.json`](run_artifacts/shared_kv_compressed_tile_sweep_20260601/summary.json) keeps H64/N64 as the retained point at `10.997 ms`; H64/N128 and H64/N256 are slightly slower, H64/N32 regresses to `15.03 ms`, and H32/H16 head tiles regress to `28.8-41.5 ms`. This closes the simple block-shape retune branch: the remaining compressed route wall needs an algorithmic dKV/scatter/fusion change, not another H/N sweep. The deeper profile split and rocprof counter artifacts now identify the mechanism as many-to-one compressed dKV atomic accumulation, not dKV dot math: full/no-dKV/checksum-sink splits put top-k512 dKV dot math near `0.79 ms` and atomic accumulation near `8.21 ms`, and the H64/N64 counter sweep reports `16.78M` atomic wavefronts plus `402.52M` TCC atomic 32-byte requests. A positive compressed dKV BMM floor drops S4096/top-k512 to `7.07 ms` mixed and `4.76 ms` pure BF16, while the chunked mixed sweep keeps chunk2048/chunk1024 at `7.69/7.72 ms` with peak memory `4.51/3.88 GiB`; chunk512/chunk256 bend to `8.11/9.51 ms`, showing repeated external-BMM overhead. The flat-GEMM follow-up is viable but not a major mixed-speed win: S4096 mixed is `7.05 ms`, chunk1024/chunk512 are `7.69/7.78 ms`, and pure BF16 passes S128 tolerance then times S4096 at `4.73 ms` with `4.10 GiB`. See [`run_artifacts/sparse_mla_sharedkv_compressed_route_mechanism_inspection_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/sparse_mla_sharedkv_compressed_route_mechanism_inspection_20260602.json), [`run_artifacts/sharedkv_compressed_dkv_bmm_floor_chunk_sweep_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/sharedkv_compressed_dkv_bmm_floor_chunk_sweep_20260602.json), and [`run_artifacts/sharedkv_compressed_dkv_flat_gemm_floor_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/sharedkv_compressed_dkv_flat_gemm_floor_summary_20260602.json). The contaminated concurrent attempt remains explicitly discarded; the retained evidence is the later clean sequential run.
- Actual LightningIndexer route fan-in refresh: [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_sharedkv_actual_li_route_fanin_s4096_layer2_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_sharedkv_actual_li_route_fanin_s4096_layer2_20260602.json) and [`run_artifacts/torchtitan_sharedkv_actual_li_route_fanin_s4096_layer3_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/torchtitan_sharedkv_actual_li_route_fanin_s4096_layer3_20260602.json) compare the real TorchTitan-shaped LI top-k routes against the earlier synthetic prefix route. Layer 2 (`CR=4`, `topk=512`) keeps the same `1,572,352` total compressed selections and the same `805M` H64 dKV atomic-add estimate, but spreads them over all `1024` compressed groups instead of the prefix route's `512` nonzero groups. Layer 3 (`CR=128`, `topk=32`) exactly matches the prefix topology because all valid compressed groups are selected. So layer 2 is the dynamic-route hard case for the fused sparse-attention backward; layer 3 can use the simpler all-group/prefix-like accumulation shape.
- Actual-LI dense-route dKV floor: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_dense_route_dkv_floor_s4096_layer2_bmm_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_dense_route_dkv_floor_s4096_layer2_bmm_20260602.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_dense_route_dkv_floor_s4096_layer2_flat_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_dense_route_dkv_floor_s4096_layer2_flat_20260602.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_dense_route_dkv_floor_s4096_layer2_bmm_chunk1024_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_dense_route_dkv_floor_s4096_layer2_bmm_chunk1024_20260602.json), and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_dense_route_dkv_floor_s4096_layer3_bmm_atol0p6_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_dense_route_dkv_floor_s4096_layer3_bmm_atol0p6_20260602.json) test whether real LI routes can be made MFMA-shaped by materializing dense route-weight matrices. Layer 2 is negative: dense-route BMM is correct but `25.22 ms` with `7.62 GiB` peak, flat GEMM is `23.14 ms`, and chunk1024 is still `23.86 ms` despite lower `3.79 GiB` peak. Layer 3 is small/easy at `3.27 ms`, matching the all-valid topology. The next layer-2 attention kernel should therefore avoid dense `[H,S,G]` route materialization and instead use sparse route-bucketed/segmented accumulation or fused partial reductions that preserve query-major reuse while reducing global dKV atomics.
- Actual-LI bucketed dKV reduce probe: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_bucket_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer2_br512_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_bucket_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer2_br512_20260602.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_bucket_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer2_br1024_seq1_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_bucket_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer2_br1024_seq1_20260602.json), and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_bucket_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer3_br512_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_bucket_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer3_br512_20260602.json) test the next obvious sparse branch: sort valid `(token, compressed_group)` pairs, then reduce per group before writing dKV. Route sorting is cheap (`0.78-1.12 ms` for layer 2), but the group-major row-wise recompute kernel is decisively negative: layer 2 passes parity at `block_rows=512` but takes `458.55 ms`, and a sequential `block_rows=1024` timing-only check is `2785.64 ms`; layer 3 passes but still takes `19.40 ms`. A D16 version closes the tempting "same idea, smaller D block" branch: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_bucket_reduce_dkv_s128_layer2_br512_bd16_dot128_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_bucket_reduce_dkv_s128_layer2_br512_bd16_dot128_20260602.json) passes S128 parity, but already takes `13.99 ms`, and the target-shape timing-only run [`run_artifacts/actual_li_bucket_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer2_br512_bd16_dot128_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_bucket_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer2_br512_bd16_dot128_20260602.json) takes `12,179 ms`. The lesson is sharper than "do not bucket": do not switch the whole backward to group-major row-wise QK/dO.V, and do not apply D16 outside the query-major/tile-local MFMA schedule. The next candidate should preserve the query-major selected-key schedule and change only the dKV write path, for example by reducing inside the query-major tile or by fusing LI/compressor backward around query-major partial reductions.
- Actual-LI compact partial-reduce floor: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_partial_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer2_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_partial_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer2_20260602.json), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_partial_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer2_correctness_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_partial_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer2_correctness_20260602.json), and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_partial_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer3_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_partial_reduce_dkv_s4096_layer3_20260602.json) test the other half of that idea: produce compact selected dKV partials query-major, then reduce by compressed group. Layer 2 correctness passes with max diff `0.0296`, but timing is still negative: selected-partial production is `15.84 ms` with `18.34 GiB` peak, flat `index_add` reduction is `2.77 ms`, `segment_reduce` is `3.01 ms`, and sort+index_add is `4.48 ms`. Layer 3 passes and is small (`2.75 ms` production, `0.176 ms` index_add), but segment_reduce is still slower. This rules out materialized compact partials as the next production path; the viable kernel should reduce dKV inside the query-major tile or fuse LI/compressor gradients before writing, without writing a 3 GiB partial buffer.
- Actual-LI tile-local coalescing estimate: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_coalescing_s4096_layer2_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_coalescing_s4096_layer2_20260602.json) and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_coalescing_s4096_layer3_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_coalescing_s4096_layer3_20260602.json) quantify how much dKV atomic traffic could be collapsed inside query-major tiles before global writes. Layer 2 has zero duplicate selected groups per token, so one-query tiles cannot coalesce at all; a small query-major-like tile (`token_block=4`, `selected_block=128`) only gives `1.43x` reduction, shrinking the H64 atomic estimate from `805M` to `565M` elements. Very wide tiles (`token_block=64`, `selected_block=512`) could give `47.25x`, but the refreshed tile-budget analyzer shows this stretch shape has `1024` selected-key microsteps per D-block tile and `2.10M` layer-level microsteps. Layer 3 is easier: `token_block=4`, `selected_block=32` gives `3.99x`, and `token_block=64` gives `62.03x`, matching the earlier all-valid topology read. The tile-budget follow-up [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_budget_s4096_layer2_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_budget_s4096_layer2_20260602.json) and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_budget_s4096_layer3_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_budget_s4096_layer3_20260602.json) now includes implementation-pressure metrics and promotes a more executable hard layer-2 first candidate: `token_block=32`, `selected_block=512`, `d_block=16`, `micro_selected=64`, with `23.81x` H64 dKV write reduction, `~115.26 KiB` p99 combined scratch under the 128 KiB budget, and `256` microsteps per D-block tile. The refreshed LDS/hash-scatter read [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_budget_lds_hash_candidate_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_budget_lds_hash_candidate_summary_20260602.json), built from [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_coalescing_s4096_layer2_tb1-64_sb32-512_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_coalescing_s4096_layer2_tb1-64_sb32-512_20260602.json) and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_budget_s4096_layer2_tb1-64_sb32-512_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_budget_s4096_layer2_tb1-64_sb32-512_20260602.json), keeps `32x512/D16` as the primary production target and selects `32x256/D16` as the lower-pressure bring-up rung: `12.34x` write reduction, `~115.39 KiB` p99 combined scratch, and `128` microsteps per D-block tile. The compact schedule contract is [`run_artifacts/actual_li_dblocked_dkv_kernel_contract_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_dblocked_dkv_kernel_contract_20260602.json). A stats-only fixed-panel follow-up [`run_artifacts/actual_li_panel_density_sweep_s4096_layer2_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_panel_density_sweep_s4096_layer2_20260602.json) shows the simpler fixed-panel branch is not rejected by density alone: at `seq_chunk=32`, `group_panel=64` has `1.417x` dense-slot overhead with `1088` nonempty panels and `group_panel=128` has `1.500x` overhead with `576` panels, while `group_panel=512` wastes `2.001x` dense slots. The executable fixed-panel Triton write-path probe [`run_artifacts/actual_li_fixed_panel_triton_dkv_sweep_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_fixed_panel_triton_dkv_sweep_20260602.json) is parity-clean but rejects both dense-panel implementation shapes tried so far: scalar-loop S512 layer 2 is `3.08 ms` for the accumulator alone versus `1.58 ms` for the materialized PyTorch reference, and the `tl.dot`-over-heads follow-up regresses to `37.22 ms` at S512 for the small-panel shape. The dynamic unique-group BMM floor [`run_artifacts/actual_li_unique_bmm_dkv_floor_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_unique_bmm_dkv_floor_summary_20260602.json) confirms the density motivation but rejects an external PyTorch bridge: S4096 layer 2 compacts to `1.344x` dense-slot overhead, but S128 already takes `8.06 ms` and S4096 timing-only takes `3220 ms`. The hard layer-2 path therefore points to in-kernel dynamic unique-group D16 compaction or deeper LI/compressor fusion; fixed panels should only be retried if the kernel compacts active groups/columns inside the tile.
- Actual-LI tile-segment ScatterAdd smoke: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_full_d_scalar_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_full_d_scalar_decision_20260603.json) adds an opt-in HIP branch to [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator.py) that prepackages valid `(token, selected-slot)` rows by tile-local compressed group and lets one CTA emit one reduced full-D row. The branch validates the segment contract: S128 passes with max diff `4.29e-5` at `1.39 ms`, and S512 passes with max diff `6.68e-5` at `1.42 ms`, beating the `3.08 ms` S512 scalar-local rejection gate. It is rejected as the S4096 production shape: the hard layer-2 `32x512` run realizes the modeled `23.81x` write reduction but takes `44.58 ms` versus the `8.806 ms` sparse-atomic wall, and `512` CTA threads regresses to `60.39 ms`. Keep the segment metadata and reduced-write target; the next kernel must keep query-major/MFMA contribution math and add tile-local grouped or segmented accumulation before global writes, not recompute H64 contributions scalar inside one segment CTA.
- Actual-LI tile-segment token-reuse check: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_token_reuse_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_token_reuse_decision_20260603.json) and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_token_reuse_s4096_layer2_tb32_sb256-512_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_segment_token_reuse_s4096_layer2_tb32_sb256-512_20260603.json) explain why the attractive segment write-reduction contract has not translated into S4096 speed. For both practical rungs, `32x256` and `32x512`, duplicate-token reuse inside a compressed-group segment is exactly zero: `overall_pair_over_unique_token_x=1.0`, `duplicate_token_segments=0`, and `max_pairs_per_token_per_segment=1`. So a group-owned segment CTA gets good ScatterAdd segments but loses the query-major KxH by HxD reuse, because every segment row comes from a different token. Decision: keep segment metadata for the final reducer, but reject moving contribution production ownership to compressed-group segments unless the kernel preserves token-local q/dO reuse.
- Actual-LI pair-slot reduced-atomic rocWMMA rung: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_rocwmma_route_grid_pairslot_atomic_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_rocwmma_route_grid_pairslot_atomic_decision_20260603.json) adds an opt-in `compact_pairslot_atomic` branch to the route-grid probe. It precomputes `pair_slots[S,K]`, keeps the query-major rocWMMA contribution producer, accumulates into compact active-group slots in LDS, and emits reduced global atomics directly. S128 and S512 pass parity and improve grouped atomic modestly (`0.124` vs `0.131 ms`; `0.527` vs `0.585 ms`). The hard S4096 layer-2 run preserves the `23.813x` modeled write reduction and improves grouped atomic (`18.45` vs `20.89 ms`), but it is still rejected against the `8.806 ms` sparse-atomic wall. This validates the pre-reduce-before-scatter direction but shows metadata/slot lookup cleanup alone is not enough; the next kernel needs lane/warp-level segmented accumulation that avoids dense active-slot initialization and per-contribution LDS stores, or a group-owned cooperative schedule that preserves token-local Q reuse without scalar segment recompute.
- Actual-LI pair-slot block-shape sweep: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_rocwmma_route_grid_pairslot_shape_sweep_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_rocwmma_route_grid_pairslot_shape_sweep_20260603.json) rejects simple `token_block`/`selected_block` tuning of the same pair-slot LDS reducer. S4096 layer-2 timings stay nearly flat while modeled write reduction varies widely: `16x256` is `19.57 ms` at `6.22x`, `16x512` is `18.54 ms` at `11.95x`, `32x256` is `18.60 ms` at `12.34x`, `64x256` is best at `18.28 ms` with `24.47x`, and `64x512` is `18.48 ms` despite `47.25x`. The residual is therefore dominated by the per-contribution LDS accumulation/CTA schedule, not just active-row count or global write volume. The next reducer must change the inner loop, for example with lane/warp segmented reductions, register-owned small segment accumulators, or a group-owned cooperative schedule that keeps query-major Q/dO reuse.
- Actual-LI pair-slot compact-partial follow-up: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_rocwmma_route_grid_pairslot_partial_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_rocwmma_route_grid_pairslot_partial_decision_20260603.json) changes the same pair-slot route-grid branch from final global atomics to compact partial rows plus `index_add`. Small shapes are positive and parity-clean against the raw kernel: S128 `0.118 ms` emit+reduce vs `0.158 ms` raw, and S512 `0.513 ms` vs `0.723 ms`. The target S4096 layer-2 run is rejected: raw atomic is `10.024 ms`, compact pair-slot atomic is `18.388 ms`, and compact pair-slot partial emit+reduce is `18.314 ms`, with raw-vs-partial max diff `1.22e-4`. The missing selected-tile sweep in [`run_artifacts/actual_li_rocwmma_route_grid_pairslot_partial_shape_sweep_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_rocwmma_route_grid_pairslot_partial_shape_sweep_20260603.json) closes the obvious "make the LDS table smaller" branch: `selected_block=64/128/512` gives compact partial emit+reduce `19.47/18.59/18.31 ms`, all behind same-probe raw `9.42-10.02 ms` and the retained Triton sparse-atomic gate `8.19 ms`. This confirms that the final reducer is not the expensive part; the producer/local pair-slot accumulation body is. Keep the compact-row contract and the fast rocPRIM reducer floor, but do not retry this exact pair-slot partial body with block-shape sweeps.
- Actual-LI compact direct-valid route-grid check: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_rocwmma_route_grid_compact_direct_valid_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_rocwmma_route_grid_compact_direct_valid_decision_20260603.json) closes the tempting "the local LDS atomicAdd is the only wall" hypothesis. The measured valid-K16 uniqueness contract holds at S128/S512/S4096, so replacing local `atomicAdd` with direct `+=` is correct for this diagnostic branch. It still loses: S512 direct-valid compact partial emit+reduce is `0.731 ms` versus grouped atomic `0.591 ms`, and S4096 is `22.61 ms` versus grouped atomic `20.90 ms` and the retained active-list atomic gate near `8.8 ms`. The wall is the route-grid body and active-slot initialization/emission pattern, not merely the local atomic primitive; the next branch needs a different segmented/group-owned topology.
- Actual-LI split-producer compact-partial reducer plan: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/plan_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_reducer.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/plan_sparse_dkv_compact_partial_reducer.py) and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_compact_partial_reducer_plan_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_compact_partial_reducer_plan_20260603.json) size the middle ground after the pair-slot rejection. This is metadata-only, not a speed result: the hard layer-2 S4096 route has `1,572,352` valid pairs, `805M` raw selected dKV scalar writes, and a `3071 MiB` raw FP32 value stream. A split producer/reducer would emit compact touched-group D16 rows; `64x512` has the best traffic model (`47.25x` write reduction, `69.2 MiB` partial stream) but likely repeats the wide-tile serialization failure, while `32x512` (`23.81x`, `137.1 MiB`, `4096` producer CTAs) and `32x256` (`12.34x`, `264.6 MiB`, `8192` producer CTAs) are the practical first kernel rungs. The promotion gate is unchanged: the real segmented reducer must beat the `8.43-8.81 ms` sparse-atomic dKV sub-slice without materializing selected K/V, probabilities, dense routes, or multi-GiB partial slabs.
- Actual-LI compact-partial rocPRIM reducer floor: [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_rocprim_vec16_compact_partial_32x512_s4096_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_rocprim_vec16_compact_partial_32x512_s4096_decision_20260603.json) turns the `32x512` split-producer plan into a real reducer primitive timing. Encoding `(compressed_group, D16 block)` into `32768` keys and reducing `2.11M` compact D16 rows, sorted reduce-only is `0.438 ms`; even random sort+value-reorder+reduce is `1.108 ms`. Ignore the tool's automatic full-D extrapolation fields for these two artifacts because the key space already covers all `32` D16 blocks. Decision: the final compact reducer is viable; the remaining blocker is a producer that emits compact rows cheaply while preserving the fast query-major dot-K/MFMA schedule, without the `18 ms` pair-slot LDS body or the `133 ms` persistent-CTA body.
- Actual-LI dot-K compact partial-store measured rung: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_dkv_active_list_triton.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_dkv_active_list_triton.py) now adds `--kernel dot_k_compact_partial_store`, preserving the fast `dot_k_atomic` producer while writing compact per-seq-tile active-group D16 partial rows before a final `index_add` fold. S128 and S512 layer-2 parity pass in [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_partial_store_s128_layer2_sc16_d16h64k32_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_partial_store_s128_layer2_sc16_d16h64k32_20260603.json) and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_partial_store_s512_layer2_sc32_d16h64k64_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_partial_store_s512_layer2_sc32_d16h64k64_20260603.json), at `0.180/0.348 ms` with max diff `0.0697/0.0717`. The refreshed S4096 layer-2 seq-chunk sweep in [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_partial_store_seqchunk_sweep_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_compact_partial_store_seqchunk_sweep_20260603.json) closes the obvious width knob: `seq_chunk=16/32/64/128` full medians are `8.364/8.541/10.280/10.325 ms`, emit-only medians are `7.945/8.273/8.665/8.881 ms`, and partial-slab elements shrink from `67.4M` to `8.65M` as the chunk widens. The same-tuple 10-sample sparse-atomic gate [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_atomic_triton_dkv_s4096_layer2_sc32_d16h64k64_timing10_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_atomic_triton_dkv_s4096_layer2_sc32_d16h64k64_timing10_20260603.json) is still faster at `8.007 ms` median. Decision: keep compact partial-store as memory/contract evidence, not a latency promotion; the next branch must fuse the reducer into the fast producer with register/warp/tile-local segmented accumulation or LI/compressor fusion rather than global compact partial load/store plus `index_add`.
- Actual-LI in-producer window-reduction planner: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/plan_sparse_dkv_inproducer_window_reduction.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/plan_sparse_dkv_inproducer_window_reduction.py) tests whether the existing fast `dot_k_atomic` loop can cheaply reduce before global writes. S128 smoke [`run_artifacts/actual_li_inproducer_window_reduction_plan_s128_layer2_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_inproducer_window_reduction_plan_s128_layer2_20260603.json) passes the route build and shows the pattern: same-slot reduction is only `1.39x`, while full local segmentation reaches `14.0x`. The hard S4096 layer-2 narrow plan [`run_artifacts/actual_li_inproducer_window_reduction_plan_s4096_layer2_narrow_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_inproducer_window_reduction_plan_s4096_layer2_narrow_20260603.json) is more decisive: for the current producer-like `token_window=32`, `selected_block=64`, cheap same-slot accumulation is only `1.034x`, and true full segmentation within `K64` is only `3.428x`; the `23.813x` target appears only when local segmentation spans `token_window=32`, `selected_block=512`. Decision: do not implement a per-K-column or per-`K64` reducer as the next production branch. To reach the modeled write reduction, the kernel must either hold a larger `K512` route window with segmented accumulation, split that wide segmentation across waves/CTAs without recomputing contribution math, or fuse LI/compressor dKV accumulation so the producer no longer emits one row per selected slot.
- Actual-LI group-owned dKV schedule planner: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/plan_sparse_dkv_group_owned_schedule.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/plan_sparse_dkv_group_owned_schedule.py), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_group_owned_sparse_dkv_schedule_plan_s4096_layer2_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_group_owned_sparse_dkv_schedule_plan_s4096_layer2_20260603.json), and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_group_owned_sparse_dkv_schedule_plan_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_group_owned_sparse_dkv_schedule_plan_decision_20260603.json) size the next non-naive version of that idea on the real hard layer-2 LI route. This is metadata-only, not a HIP timing result. The route has `1,572,352` valid pairs and the same `805M` raw H64 dKV atomic-add elements as the sparse-atomic gate (`8.007 ms`). The useful envelope is positive: `token_block=32, group_panel=256` models `23.81x` write reduction with `0.958` K16 fill and `137.15 MiB` active stream, while `token_block=64, group_panel=256` models `47.25x` write reduction with the same K16 fill and `69.18 MiB` active stream. The important blocker is route ownership, not density: `group_panel=128/256/512` would imply `8x/4x/2x` naive top-k rescans, so the next runtime kernel must prepack routes or build an equivalent in-producer segmented path before the group-owned K16 accumulator. Do not prototype a naive panel-rescan kernel; first S128/S512 gate should be `token_block=32, group_panel=256`, then compare S4096 against the `8.0-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic dKV slice without selected K/V, dense routes, or multi-GiB partial slabs.
- Actual-LI group-panel route-pack timing: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_dkv_group_panel_route_pack.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_dkv_group_panel_route_pack.py), [`run_artifacts/actual_li_group_panel_route_pack_s4096_layer2_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_group_panel_route_pack_s4096_layer2_20260603.json), and [`run_artifacts/actual_li_group_panel_route_pack_decision_20260603.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_group_panel_route_pack_decision_20260603.json) measure the route-list contract required by the group-owned accumulator: valid `(token, selected-slot)` entries sorted by `(seq_tile, group_panel, token)`. This is still route metadata only, not dKV math. The important result is positive: even a Torch sort-based pack is `~0.52-0.54 ms` event median over all tested `token_block=32/64` and `group_panel=128/256/512` rows, comfortably below the `8.0-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic dKV wall. The retained safe bring-up row remains `token_block=32, group_panel=256`: `0.527 ms` pack, `23.81x` modeled write reduction, `0.958` K16 fill, `10,225` token-panel segments, and `~12.0 MiB` int32 route-list workspace. The higher-reduction follow-up is `token_block=64, group_panel=256/512`: `0.526/0.523 ms` pack and `47.25x` modeled write reduction. Decision: prepacking is viable; the next risk is the HIP/CK/rocWMMA accumulator body consuming `pair_pos_sorted + group_ids_sorted + token_panel_starts` without the scalar/local-table overhead that killed the previous reducers.
- Actual-LI active-group detection and packing probe: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_active_groups_triton.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_active_groups_triton.py) isolates the route-compaction metadata step needed by the dynamic unique-group D16 path. The first summary [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_groups_triton_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_groups_triton_summary_20260602.json) shows exact S128 and S4096 mask/count parity. The compact-list follow-up [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_groups_pack_triton_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_groups_pack_triton_summary_20260602.json) adds a Triton pack kernel that converts flags/counts into sorted active compressed-group lists per query tile. On the hard S4096 layer-2 route, the retained `seq_chunk=32`, `group_block=64`, `selected_block=64` point passes exact flag/count/list parity; flags-only is `0.858 ms`, pack-only is `0.0356 ms`, and flags+pack is `0.848 ms`, with the same `1.344x` compact dense-slot overhead and `66,029` unique groups across `128` query tiles. Layer 3 remains the easy contrast at `0.0686 ms` flags+pack and `1.016x` overhead. So full route metadata is cheap enough to keep the in-kernel dynamic-compaction branch alive; the missing piece is still the D16 dKV accumulator itself.
- Actual-LI active-list D16 dKV accumulator probe: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_dkv_active_list_triton.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_dkv_active_list_triton.py) consumes the packed active-group lists plus materialized `probs`/`grad_logits` to isolate only the reduced-write accumulator body. The consolidated result [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json) keeps the metadata path but does not promote this scalar active-list accumulator: S128 layer 2 passes parity and is competitive (`0.386 ms` best vs `0.478 ms` PyTorch reference), but S512 layer 2 regresses as the active-list loop grows (`3.134 ms` best at `block_u=128` vs `1.574 ms` PyTorch reference, with `7.508 ms` at `block_u=32`). The next sparse-attention backward kernel should keep exact active-list packing, but replace this body with a HIP/CK-Tile-style streaming D16 schedule or fuse LI/compressor gradients before global dKV writes.
- Actual-LI active-list dot-K dKV accumulator probe: the same tool now has `--kernel dot_k`, which batches selected keys before routing them into active compressed groups. The summary [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json) is a useful partial win: S128 layer 2 drops to `0.137 ms`, and S512 layer 2 drops to `0.416 ms` at `block_k=32/64`, beating the materialized PyTorch reference around `1.58 ms` and the scalar active-list `3.134 ms`. But S4096 layer 2 is rejected for this dense route-dot body: the hard route has `515.9` mean and `1024` max active groups per tile, so `route[active_group,K] @ contrib[K,D]` becomes dense over hundreds of rows. The best timing-only target-shape point is still `47.26 ms` (`seq_chunk=64`, `block_u=512`, `block_k=64`), far slower than the current query-major full atomic slice at `11.081 ms`. Keep dot-K selected-key batching as a sub-mechanism, but the production S4096 layer-2 path needs sparse/segmented route accumulation or deeper LI/compressor fusion, not a dense active-group route matrix.
- Actual-LI active-list dot-K sparse-atomic dKV accumulator probe: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_atomic_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_atomic_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json) adds `--kernel dot_k_atomic`, which keeps the selected-key dot-K body but writes one `KxD` contribution for every valid selected compressed group with direct global atomics instead of building `route[active_group,K]`. This confirms the dense route matrix was the `dot_k` S4096 failure mode: S128 layer 2 passes at `0.147 ms`, S512 layer 2 passes at `0.272 ms`, and the hard S4096 layer-2 timing-only best is `8.806 ms` at `block_k=64` (`K32` is `9.539 ms`, `K128` is `11.666 ms`). The rocprof trace summary [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_atomic_rocprof_s4096_kernel_trace_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_atomic_rocprof_s4096_kernel_trace_20260602.json) confirms the target kernel itself at `8.614 ms`; the in-probe `135.95 ms` CUDA-event timing from that profiled run is explicitly discarded as profiler contamination. The corrected accounting is important: this kernel's actual write reduction is `1.0x`; the `23.813x` number is only the coalesced active-list target (`805,044,224 -> 33,806,848` scalar dKV elements), not achieved by `dot_k_atomic`. So the next sparse-attention backward step is not more dot-K tuning; it is in-tile sparse/segmented dKV reduction or LI/compressor fusion before global writes.
- Actual-LI dot-K partial-store writepath check: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_partial_store_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_partial_store_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json) tests whether the `8-9 ms` S4096 wall is mostly cross-tile global-atomic contention. It keeps the fast selected-key `tl.dot` body from `dot_k_atomic`, but writes into dense `[seq_tile, compressed_group, D]` partial rows before reducing across sequence tiles. S128 and S512 pass at `0.110 ms` and `0.300 ms`, respectively. The hard S4096 layer-2 emit-only timing is `8.795 ms`, almost identical to `dot_k_atomic` at `8.806 ms`, and full partial+reduce is `9.507 ms`. This closes the cross-tile-contention hypothesis: splitting destinations removes final global atomics but still writes the raw `805M` KxD contribution elements, so the production path must reduce repeated compressed-group contributions inside the tile before global memory.
- Actual-LI micro-active dot-K check: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_micro_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_micro_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json) tests whether active groups compacted per selected-key block can keep the fast dense-route `tl.dot` mechanism while reducing writes. This is positive only at short sequence: S128 passes at `0.105 ms` with `14.0x` modeled write reduction, and S512 passes at `0.307 ms` with `17.5x` reduction. The hard S4096 layer-2 route rejects the idea: `K64/U128` is `60.67 ms`, `K128/U256` is `57.24 ms`, `K256/U512` exceeds MI350 shared-memory limits (`262 KiB` required versus `160 KiB` limit), and `K256/U256` regresses to `124.84 ms`. The route lists are still hundreds of groups wide per microtile at S4096, so this branch retires Triton micro-active dense route-dot as the production path.
- Actual-LI active-list dot-K sparse-local dKV accumulator probe: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_sparse_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_sparse_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json) adds `--kernel dot_k_sparse`, which keeps selected-key batched `tl.dot`, avoids the dense route matrix, and accumulates one output row per active compressed group before global writes. It achieves the coalesced write accounting at S128/S512, but this is the wrong compute shape: S128 passes at `0.431 ms` with `14.0x` write reduction, while S512 passes at `8.226 ms` with `30.0x` write reduction, far slower than `dot_k_atomic` (`0.272 ms`) and dense-route `dot_k` (`0.416 ms`) at the same S512 shape. S4096 is skipped because S512 already rejects scalar local sparse accumulation. The retained direction is true segmented/MFMA-friendly streaming reduction or LI/compressor fusion, not per-selected local active-list accumulation in Triton.
- Actual-LI active-list dot-K slot-sparse mechanism check: [`run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_slot_sparse_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_active_list_dotk_slot_sparse_triton_dkv_summary_20260602.json) adds `--kernel dot_k_slot_sparse`, which precomputes each selected route entry's active-list row slot before the Triton accumulator. This isolates whether the `dot_k_sparse` wall was row lookup or the accumulation body. It improves only slightly: S128 is `0.393 ms` versus `0.431 ms`, and S512 is `8.062 ms` versus `8.226 ms`. That retires active-row lookup cleanup as the next lever; the scalar per-selected local accumulation loop is the wall.
- Compressed-dKV segmented backend decision: [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_backend_options_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_backend_options_20260602.json) records the MI350 image/toolchain surface for the next accumulator branch. `onenexus/nexus-titan:rocm722-pytorch-nightly-mori` has Triton/AITER/MORI plus ROCm `rocprim`, `hipcub`, `ck`, and `ck_tile` headers, but no TileLang Python package. A `hipcc --offload-arch=gfx950` smoke compiles CK-Tile plus rocPRIM/hipCUB segmented-reduction headers cleanly, and the PyTorch HIP extension smoke [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_extension_smoke_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_extension_smoke_20260602.json) builds/calls a CK-Tile/rocPRIM/hipCUB-including extension on `AMD Instinct MI350X VF` with max diff `0.0`. AITER's inspected reductions are MoE/serving-style row reductions rather than this sparse-attention training dKV contraction. So the next production-surface branch should be a gfx950 HIP/CK-Tile/rocPRIM segmented accumulator, with Triton kept for route metadata and small probes, not another Triton row-lookup cleanup.
- Compressed-dKV rocPRIM reduce-by-key floor: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_rocprim_reduce_by_key.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_rocprim_reduce_by_key.py) isolates the scalar reduction primitive for keys `compressed_group * d_tile + d`, summarized in [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_rocprim_reduce_by_key_decision_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_rocprim_reduce_by_key_decision_20260602.json). S512 sorted and random-sort smokes both pass parity (`9.54e-6` and `1.14e-5` max diff). At the S4096 layer-2 valid-pair proxy (`1,572,864` route pairs, `25,165,824` scalar D16 items), already-sorted keys reduce in `0.111 ms` for one D16 tile, extrapolating to `3.54 ms` over D512, so rocPRIM reduction itself is not the wall. But random scalar sort plus value reorder plus reduce is `1.433 ms` for one D16 tile, extrapolating to `45.86 ms` over D512, which rejects scalar global sort/reduce as a production route. The useful next branch is a custom query-major D16 grouped/segmented accumulator that reuses pair-level route order or groups inside the tile, not a framework-level scalar sort per D tile.
- Compressed-dKV rocPRIM Vec16 reduce-by-key follow-up: [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_rocprim_vec16_reduce_by_key_decision_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_rocprim_vec16_reduce_by_key_decision_20260602.json) extends the same probe to sort route pairs once and reduce a `float32[16]` value payload keyed only by `compressed_group`. S512 random parity passes with max diff `9.54e-6`. Pair-level sorting helps versus scalar global sort: S4096 random sort+reorder+reduce extrapolates to `26.73 ms` over D512 instead of scalar's `45.86 ms`. But generic rocPRIM Vec16 reduction is too expensive as a standalone production body: S4096 already-sorted Vec16 reduce extrapolates to `10.20 ms` over D512, worse than scalar's `3.54 ms` reduce-only floor and still above the current `8.6-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic dKV wall. The retained lesson is to reuse/produce pair-level route order, but implement the final reducer as a CK-Tile/MFMA-friendly segmented or split-wave/CTA grouped body rather than a generic Vec16 `reduce_by_key`.
- Compressed-dKV HIP accumulator smoke: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator.py) is the first actual accumulator through that extension surface. It consumes the same materialized `probs`/`grad_logits` plus active-group lists as the Triton active-list diagnostic and writes the real `grad_kv` tensor. S128 layer 2 passes with max diff `3.62e-5` and median `0.488 ms` in [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator_s128_layer2_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator_s128_layer2_20260602.json). S512 layer 2 also passes parity with max diff `6.48e-5`, but the scalar HIP loop is rejected at median `7.396 ms` versus Triton scalar `3.233 ms` and PyTorch materialized reference `1.584 ms`; see [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator_s512_layer2_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator_s512_layer2_20260602.json). The no-global-atomic tile-partial follow-up also passes but is still `7.281 ms` at S512, essentially unchanged from scalar atomic, in [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator_tilepartial_s512_layer2_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator_tilepartial_s512_layer2_20260602.json). Keep the HIP extension surface; replace the body with a CK-Tile/MFMA-friendly selected-key contraction plus in-tile segmented schedule before attempting S4096.
- Actual-LI tile-local coalesced dKV oracle: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_dkv_tile_coalesced.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/benchmark_sparse_mla_shared_kv_actual_li_dkv_tile_coalesced.py) is the first executable correctness harness for that D16 contract. On MI350, the S128 layer-2 parity artifact [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_coalesced_dkv_s128_layer2_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_coalesced_dkv_s128_layer2_20260602.json) passes against the current shared-KV dKV reference with max diff `1.72e-5` and identical norm, while reducing modeled H64 dKV write elements `1,032,192 -> 40,960` (`25.2x`) for the small route. The target-shape stats-only capture [`run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_coalesced_dkv_stats_s4096_layer2_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/actual_li_tile_coalesced_dkv_stats_s4096_layer2_20260602.json) rebuilds the actual TorchTitan-shaped S4096 layer-2 LI route and confirms the pressure-balanced counters exactly: `805,044,224 -> 33,806,848` modeled H64 dKV write elements (`23.813x`). This is not a performance kernel yet; Python tile loops and `torch.unique` make it an oracle for the next HIP/CK-Tile/Triton implementation.
- Compressed dKV dense-group HIP reducer: [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_dense_group_tile_decision_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_dense_group_tile_decision_20260602.json) turns the coalesced-write oracle into a first HIP runtime probe. The important correction is that `23.813x` is only the modeled global write reduction (`805,044,224 -> 33,806,848` scalar dKV elements), not a speedup. A dense local compressed-group x D16 LDS table passes parity at S128 and S512; S512 improves scalar HIP `7.50 ms -> 4.14 ms`, but still trails the materialized PyTorch/GEMM reference `1.58 ms`. The S4096 `selected_block=256` timing-only rung realizes an `11.91x` modeled write reduction but takes `121.8 ms`; the rocprof trace [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_dense_group_tile_rocprof_s4096_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_dense_group_tile_rocprof_s4096_20260602.json) confirms the HIP kernel itself is `120.07 ms` and `87.5%` of traced kernel time. Scalar LDS accumulation is therefore rejected as a production path. The retained next step is a CK-Tile/MFMA-style segmented reducer that preserves query-major selected-key reuse, avoids dense route materialization, and performs local dKV reduction before global writes.
- Next compressed-dKV reducer contract: [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_mfma_segmented_reducer_next_contract_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_mfma_segmented_reducer_next_contract_20260602.json) makes the post-rejection implementation ladder explicit. The `121.8 ms` dense-group HIP result is not a full-layer regression; it rejects a scalar local-accumulation body. The first executable rung is `token_block=32`, `selected_block=256`, `head_block=64`, `d_block=16`, `micro_selected=64`, with `12.34x` modeled write reduction and `~115.39 KiB` p99 scratch. The primary target widens to `32x512/D16` for the full `23.813x` write-reduction contract. Promotion requires S128/S512 parity, no selected-K/V or score/prob/route slab materialization at S4096, S512 beating the rejected scalar local branches, and S4096 beating the `8.6-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic wall before fusing LI/compressor gradients.
- Contract-rung S512 gate: [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator_densegroup_s512_layer2_contract32x256_gate_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_segmented_hip_accumulator_densegroup_s512_layer2_contract32x256_gate_20260602.json) applies the `32x256/D16` smoke knobs to the scalar dense-group HIP body on one MI350. Dense-group parity passes tightly (`max_abs_diff=3.43e-5`) and write accounting collapses the S512 layer-2 route from `16.71M` raw dKV scalar elements to `0.557M` (`30.0x`), but median event time is `4.18 ms`, failing the `3.08 ms` S512 promotion gate and far behind the materialized PyTorch/GEMM context at `1.58 ms`. This confirms the problem is not only global atomic count; the body must become MFMA/CK-Tile-shaped before S4096 promotion.
- Compressed-dKV MFMA schedule pressure: [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_mfma_schedule_pressure_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_mfma_schedule_pressure_20260602.json) records the sharper mechanism after the S512 gate. `dot_k_atomic` keeps the fast `tl.dot` contribution body and is the retained S4096 sparse-atomic wall at `8.81 ms`, but writes the full `805M` selected dKV elements. `dot_k_micro` and fixed-panel-style routes reduce writes, but recompute the KxD contribution for each active-group block or group panel, so S4096 lands at `57-125 ms`. The required next kernel is therefore not another active-list route-matrix tweak: compute `contrib_kd = grad_logits^T q * scale + probs^T dO` once with MFMA-style math, then do tile-local grouped/hash/segmented accumulation before global writes. The current MI350 image has `rocwmma`, `ck_tile`, and HIP headers, and a minimal `rocwmma` `gfx950` compile smoke passes, so the next executable rung is a HIP/rocWMMA or CK-Tile contribution-tile smoke before adding local grouped accumulation.
- Compressed-dKV rocWMMA contribution-tile smoke: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_rocwmma_contrib_tile.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_rocwmma_contrib_tile.py) now passes the first PyTorch HIP-extension rung on one MI350. The extension needs PyTorch HIP half/BF16 macro undefs plus a full 64-thread AMD wavefront for rocWMMA fragments; the earlier 32-thread launch built but failed parity in [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_rocwmma_contrib_tile_w32_failure_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_rocwmma_contrib_tile_w32_failure_20260602.json). The retained run [`run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_rocwmma_contrib_tile_w64_smoke_20260602.json`](run_artifacts/compressed_dkv_rocwmma_contrib_tile_w64_smoke_20260602.json) computes `dKV[K,D] = dL_scaled[K,H] @ Q[H,D] + P[K,H] @ dO[H,D]` for a BF16 `16x16x64` tile with FP32 accumulation, max diff `2.98e-8`, and median `0.00744 ms`. This proves the MFMA-shaped contribution math surface; it still needs tile-local grouped/segmented accumulation before it can attack the S4096 `8.6-8.8 ms` sparse-atomic wall.
- Compressed-dKV rocWMMA grouped-accumulation tile smoke: [`tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_rocwmma_grouped_accum_tile.py`](tools/dsv4_runtime_probe/probe_compressed_dkv_rocwmma_grouped_accum_tile.py) adds the next in-kernel rung: compute the same selected-row contribution tile with rocWMMA, store it in LDS, reduce duplicate compressed-group rows in LDS, and write only grouped D16 rows.
